▲Instructions for Members Taking Cars

Nanjing Telegram, Instructions for members taking cars, 1. In order to facilitate the travel of members to the meeting, the conference will provide cars for transportation every day during the general assembly. The methods are as follows: (I) If there is no public banquet before the meeting, they will be picked up by the reception office to the conference venue; (II) If there is a public banquet before the meeting, they will be picked up from the banquet location to the conference venue; (III) If there is no public banquet at the end of the meeting, they will be sent back to the reception office from the conference venue; (IV) If there is a public banquet at the end of the meeting, they will be sent from the conference venue to the banquet location. 2. The conference will provide cars for members to ride during the public tour time specified by the conference. 3. Only members of this conference are allowed to ride in the cars of this conference. 4. Each car must be filled with five people before it can depart. 5. The number of cars in this conference is limited. If they need to be picked up and dropped off in multiple trips, the reception staff will decide temporarily.

▲Short-Term Spectator Tickets

Not Applicable to the Opening Ceremony

Because party and state dignitaries will participate in the opening ceremony of the conference, in order to strictly prevent and maintain the order of the venue, the conference announced that short-term spectator tickets will not be applicable to the opening ceremony.

▲Statistics on Member Qualifications

According to the conference regulations, the qualifications for membership include the Director of the Provincial Department of Education, the Director of the Special Municipality Education Bureau, one Director of the County Education Bureau per province, the President of the National University, education experts, representatives of various ministries, departments, and committees, and the staff of the Ministry of Education, seven categories. The number of members in the seven categories is counted separately as follows:

1. Twenty-three representatives of the Director of the Provincial Department of Education or representatives. Originally there were twenty-seven people, but because the four provinces of Shaanxi, Guangxi, Gansu, and Ningxia have not yet received their telegram replies, it is feared that no one will attend. Xikang Province telegraphed the Ministry of Education yesterday that they can send a representative to attend.

2. Twelve representatives of the County Education Bureau designated by the provinces. The other provinces did not designate them in advance, and it is still uncertain whether they will send representatives temporarily.

3. Eight Directors of the Special Municipality Education Bureau or representatives.

4. Fourteen Presidents of National Universities or representatives.

5. Thirty education experts.

6. Nineteen representatives of various Yuan, Ministries, and Committees of the Central Government.

7. Ten Chief Officers, Vice-Ministers, Directors, and Counselors of the Ministry of Education.

A total of 120 members. Among these 120 members, 29 live in Nanjing and 91 are from out of town.

Implementation Plan for Adult Literacy Education

Circumstances of Compilation and

Key Points by Zhong Lingxiu

According to the most recent survey, China's population is approximately 430 million, but the illiterate population accounts for 80%, roughly 300 million people. Among these, excluding school-age children subject to compulsory education, children under six years old (both around 40 million), elderly people over fifty years old (50 million), and the blind, deaf, mute, disabled, and those with mental or neurological disorders (about one million), there remain over 200 million people, accounting for about half of the total population. These are all young and adult individuals who are the sound members of the nation and the backbone of society. During this period of political tutelage, if we want to train these large numbers of ignorant people to understand Party principles, exercise the four powers, and possess basic national knowledge and life skills, then the only true way is to actively implement literacy education.

Therefore, in June of the 18th year of the Republic (1929), the First Plenary Session of the Third Central Executive Committee, in discussing the proposal for rectifying and developing national education, resolved the following two cases: (1) "Vigorously implement national compulsory education and adult literacy education, with the planning, regulations, and implementation procedures to be formulated by the Ministry of Education by the end of September of the 18th year, approved by the Central Executive Committee, and actively implemented. The entire plan must be realized by the end of the 23rd year of the Republic." (2) "Regarding measures for rectifying and developing education, the government should immediately convene a national education conference in the spring of the 19th year, organized by the Ministry of Education. Before the conference is convened, the Ministry of Education should immediately organize an Education Program Drafting Committee, based on the Party's political platform, resolutions on education from previous National Congresses, Central Plenary Sessions, Standing Committee meetings, etc., and referring to the resolutions of the National Education Conference convened by the University Council in the 17th year, to create a program for implementing the rectification and development of national education. This program must include the entire education budget. The organization of the Education Program Drafting Committee will be decided by the Central Political Council, and it must be established and begin work within July of the 18th year."

After receiving this order in July of the 18th year, the Ministry of Education, in August, hired over fifty education experts as members to establish the Education Program Drafting Committee and conduct group discussions. Those who were hired as specialized committee members for the Adult Literacy Education Group were Meng Xiancheng, Chen Jianxiao, Zhong Lingxiu, Gu Shusen, Yu Qingtang, Zhao Mian, Jiang Hengyuan, and seven others, with Meng Xiancheng as the director. However, although the members of this group were appointed, they were each occupied with other matters and it was not easy to convene meetings for discussion. Moreover, because adult literacy education fell under the purview of the first section of the Department of Social Education, and I was in charge of the section's affairs, I first drafted the general outline of this plan as follows: (1) Explanation of the Outline, (2) Estimation of the Number of People Requiring Adult Literacy Education, (3) Types of Literacy Schools, (4) School Buildings and Equipment, (5) Teacher Training, (6) Funding Sources and Fundraising Methods, (7) Timing for Implementing Compulsory Adult Literacy Education, and the Implementation Procedures by Year. After the draft was completed, it was sent to Chen Jianxiao, Director of the Department of Social Education, for review. Then, Mr. Gu Liangjie, Director Chen Jianxiao, and I took on the task of drafting the details. In September, the drafts were gradually completed, and dozens of copies were printed and distributed to the specialized committee members of adult literacy education to solicit opinions. After a month, those who submitted supplementary opinions included Mr. Meng Xiancheng, Jiang Hengyuan, Zhao Mian, and Tao Zhihing. On November 5th, it was submitted to the Second Standing Committee Meeting of the Education Program Drafting Committee for discussion. It was decided that this program would be carried out in two steps: (1) National Literacy Training, (2) Vocational Training. It was also decided to invite the original drafters, Director Chen, and myself, along with Zhu Jingnong, Tao Zhihing, and Mr. Gu Shusen, to jointly review it on the morning of November 6th. At that time, the principles of civic literacy training proposed by Mr. Tao were considered and revised, and the general outline of vocational training was drafted by Mr. Gu Shusen. On the same afternoon, it was submitted to the Third Standing Committee Meeting for discussion. The two principles were revised separately and then handed over to the original drafters, Director Chen and myself, to incorporate everyone's opinions and compile them together. At the end of December, the draft was completed and sent to Minister Jiang for review. Minister Jiang believed that the cost was too high and the state's financial resources might not be able to bear it. Therefore, it was decided to first focus on achieving national literacy training within six years of political tutelage, and to continue to conduct vocational training after literacy training was implemented. By proceeding in two steps, the state's financial resources would be easier to bear. Therefore, the title of the original plan was changed to "Preliminary Plan for Implementing Adult Literacy Education," and its content was divided into seven items: (1) Principles, (2) Current Urgent Issues, (3) Methods for Enrolling Out-of-School Adults in Literacy Classes and Training Teachers, (4) Methods for Increasing School Buildings and Equipment, (5) Budget and Fundraising Methods, (6) Methods for Compiling National Literacy Teaching Materials, (7) Procedures for Implementing Universalization, (8) Scheduled Compulsory Period and Post-Compulsory Assessment. The manuscript was completed and revised by mid-January, and dozens of copies were printed and sent by the Ministry of Education to the Executive Yuan, then to the National Government, and finally to the Central Political Council for review. This is the process of the second draft and submission of this plan to the Central Committee for review.

However, it has been two months since it was submitted to the Central Committee for review, and it has not yet been returned. The period for the National Education Conference is not far off, and when the entire improved education program is submitted, this plan will also be included to ensure its finalization. The original draft has also been slightly added to and deleted. This is also the process of submitting this plan and other complete education programs to the Central Committee for review again. In addition, although the second part, vocational training, is planned to be implemented after the first part, literacy training, is completed, if local financial and human resources are available to conduct them simultaneously, and if there is a need in this area, it can be continued. Naturally, it can be carried out simultaneously or gradually. Therefore, the vocational training plan must also be drafted. Therefore, after drafting, it will be included in the second item of the improved social education plan, so that it can be fully discussed at the National Education Conference to achieve perfection. This also needs to be explained in passing.

Speaking of the content of this plan, it can be simply divided into two major parts: (1) National Literacy Training, (2) Vocational Training. The former, if implemented according to the plan, can rescue all illiterate adults in the country within six years, truly achieving the goal of everyone being able to read, study, read newspapers, write letters, calculate, and keep accounts. The latter, if continued to be implemented according to the plan, will allow farmers, workers, women, and others to enjoy vocational training separately, naturally providing them with many necessary knowledge and skills in their lives and occupations, and increasing their various production capacities. In short, this case, if fully implemented, can indeed enrich people's lives, support social survival, develop the national economy, continue the nation's life, achieve national independence, universal economic rights, and develop people's livelihood, in order to promote the great harmony of the world. However, there are still many incomplete aspects of the plan, and the responsibility for supplementing and correcting them naturally rests with the members of this National Education Conference.

Because the National Education Conference is held today, and the Shen Bao newspaper has a special education issue, I would like to describe the process of drafting this case and its key points in order to expand the scope, and to respond to the entrustment.

A Comparison of the Second Conference and the Previous Conference by Wu Yan Yin

What are the differences between this National Education Conference's origins, organization, and proposals and the National Education Conference convened by the University Council in May of the 17th year? How much of the resolutions of the first National Education Conference has been implemented now? Are the unimplemented ones listed in the current proposals? What are the differences in the level of detail between the contents of the two proposals? These are all questions that the education community urgently wants to know. Now I would like to briefly talk about these questions.

(I) Origins

The first conference was convened shortly after the establishment of the Nanjing National Government. At that time, the Three Principles of the People's education was about to be implemented and the education administration had not yet been unified. The President of the University Council, Mr. Cai Yuanpei, and many university committee members believed that it was necessary to hold a National Education Conference. Therefore, the first conference was initiated by the University Council. This conference was convened based on the resolutions of the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee and was initiated by the Central Committee. The Central Committee believed that education was important during the period of political tutelage and that a conference should be convened to solicit the opinions of the national education community to create a complete education program and a complete education budget. Therefore, in terms of origins, the two conferences each had its own needs and its own intentions, and they were truly different.

(II) Organization

For the first conference, each province sent two members, each special municipality sent one member, and each government agency sent one delegate. In addition, there were eighteen expert members, the President, Vice President, and Secretary-General of the University Council, and the heads of various departments and counselors, totaling ten people. There were also seven or eight members of the University Committee attending. The total number was seventy or eighty people. This time, the number of provinces, special municipalities, and government agencies has increased. Therefore, although the quota is the same as last time, the total number has increased significantly. The number of expert members has also increased by twelve compared to last time. The number of department heads, deputy heads, directors, counselors, and the Ministry of Education is about the same as last time, but the presidents of national universities have replaced the university committee members to attend as attendees instead of attending members. Therefore, the total number of members is as high as one hundred and thirty-three people. What is also obviously the same is that the majority of the previous members were academic experts and university professors. The primary education community, the overseas Chinese education community, and the Mongolian-Tibetan education community did not participate. This time, in addition to three or four primary education experts, each province also has a city or county education bureau chief or city or county education section chief who is in charge of primary education administration. There are also several overseas Chinese education experts and Mongolian-Tibetan education experts. The conference period was ten days last time and seven days this time.

(III) Preparation

The organization of the preparatory committee was roughly the same for both times, but there were a few differences: (1) The number of preparatory members was smaller last time, and a few people bore too heavy a burden. This time, the number of people is larger, and if they are combined, there is a joint office, and if they are divided, they each have their own responsibilities, so that the affairs they bear will not have the disadvantage of being too light or too heavy. (2) The preparations were more complete and detailed. All matters such as reception, editing documents, and affairs that could be prepared in advance were prepared in advance. This is a natural result, because this is the second time, and many people have prepared for the first conference and already have a lot of experience. However, the period was rushed, and there were still many things that could not be handled in a relaxed manner, and the member reception area was too far from the venue and it was not easy to take care of it. This is where it is not as good as the first conference.

(IV) Proposals

The two proposals differ the most. This is the most valuable comparison. Now I will briefly describe the more important differences between the proposals in general terms below:

(I) Different Origins

Although the previous proposals were first formed by the Six Proposal Committees and prepared in advance, in addition to the proposals prepared by the Proposal Committees, there were also proposals freely submitted by various education institutions and proposals submitted by individual members and education personnel. Even the proposals prepared by the Proposal Committees were mostly submitted in the name of individual members. This time, the proposals were compiled by the Education Program Drafting Committee established by the Ministry of Education, based on the educational purpose of the Republic of China and its implementation strategy, as well as the resolutions on education made by the Central Committee in the past and the resolutions of the previous National Education Conference. They were submitted to the Central Political Council for review and approval, and were submitted without using individual names at all. There are no other proposals that can be submitted by various education institutions and individuals in the education community. Therefore, the previous proposals were produced by the free thoughts of individuals in the education community, and this time the proposals were formulated by the Central Committee and produced by the unified will of the government.

(II) Different Methods

Because of the different origins, the

The previous proposals were fragmented and mixed, and this time the proposals were whole and pure. Last time, each proposed his own case, so the opinions were very divergent. Some were repetitive, some were conflicting, some were too detailed, and some were completely lacking. This time, it is a systematic program, so it is consistent from beginning to end, there is no repetition, there are few conflicts, there are no too detailed places, and it is more complete and not lacking. In terms of form, last time there were four hundred and two cases, and this time there is only one case. Last time, each case had its own reasons and methods, and some even only had reasons and no methods. This time, it is divided into chapters and sections, listing the methods and omitting the reasons, and some do not explain any reasons at all.

(III) Different Classifications

For the convenience of reviewing the previous proposals, they were divided into twelve groups: the Three Principles of the People's education, education administration, education funding, general education, social education, higher education, physical education and military education, vocational education, science education, art education, publications and library improvement, and private schools. This time, the program is divided into a preliminary plan for implementing compulsory education, a preliminary plan for implementing adult literacy education, a plan for establishing various levels and types of teacher training institutions, a plan for improving primary education, a plan for improving secondary education, a plan for improving higher education, a plan for improving social education, a plan for improving and developing overseas Chinese education, a plan for implementing Mongolian-Tibetan education, and a total budget for the entire program, a total of ten chapters. Comparing the two, except for higher education and social education, the rest are different. This time, the program says very little about the organization of the education administration itself, and the administrative methods of each part of education are included in various programs, so they are not listed as a category. In addition to a certain amount of "total budget for the entire program" for education funding, how to raise funds was originally not the responsibility of the education community. Improving private schools is an administrative method in ordinary education and higher education. Physical education and military education, science education, art education, and publications are either related to the curriculum or to administrative facilities. Vocational education is a type of secondary education, and libraries are one end of social education or school education, so this time they are not listed as a category. Originally, improving primary education could include compulsory education, and improving social education could include adult literacy education, and improving primary, secondary, and higher education could include teacher training, and there is no need to create another chapter. So the reason for listing them separately is that the Central Committee pays special attention to popularizing education (that is, compulsory education and adult literacy education), and teacher training is most related to popularizing education. As for overseas Chinese education and Mongolian-Tibetan education, they have their own special points, so they are also listed as separate categories. In short, the classification of the two proposals is more systematic this time than last time.

(IV) Different Contents

This can be said separately. A. The previous proposals were no longer mentioned in this program because they have now been implemented as separate cases or are being promoted. These are the following:

A. Regarding the purpose of education and the strategy of education (implemented separately by the Central Committee)

B. Regarding student autonomy (implemented separately by the Central Committee)

C. Regarding the school system (sorted and implemented by the Ministry of Education as a case)

D. Regarding the supervisors of provinces and cities and counties (implemented by the Ministry of Education as a separate case)

E. Regarding the academic year and holidays (implemented by the Ministry of Education as a separate case)

F. Regarding students' uniforms and the use of domestic goods (implemented by the Ministry of Education as a case)

B. Regarding the regulations of medical school districts (unnecessary)

A. Regarding the standards for students to participate in mass movements

The previous proposals have not been implemented, and the original content or changes to the original content have been included in this program. These are the following:

A. Regarding reorganizing the normal school system and paying attention to training rural education teachers (incorporated into the plan for establishing various levels and types of teacher training institutions, changing the content)

B. Regarding overseas Chinese education (incorporated into the plan for improving and developing overseas Chinese education)

C. Regarding integrating and developing the cultures of various ethnic groups and border provinces (incorporated into the plan for implementing Mongolian-Tibetan education)

D. Regarding the implementation of national compulsory education (incorporated into the preliminary plan for implementing compulsory education, changing the content)

E. Regarding improving the treatment of elementary school teachers and staff (incorporated into the plan for improving primary education)

F. Regarding the elementary school teachers' summer vacation supplementary study methods (incorporated into the plan for improving various levels and types of teacher training institutions)

G. Regarding secondary schools seriously examining academic performance (incorporated into the plan for improving secondary education)

H. Regarding agricultural, industrial, and commercial literacy education (incorporated into the plan for improving social education)

I. Regarding improving social morality and public entertainment and public reading materials (incorporated into the plan for improving social education)

J. Regarding university graduation examinations and the granting of degrees (incorporated into the higher education plan, changing the content)

K. Regarding sending students abroad (same as above, changing the content)

L. Regarding revitalizing national sports (incorporated into the plan for improving social education)

M. Regarding using school education to supplement social education (same as above)

N. Regarding promoting vocational education and reorganizing industrial and commercial schools (incorporated into the plan for improving secondary and higher education)

In short, the previous proposals were fragmented and incomplete, and the methods were not very appropriate. This time, the program has more detailed regulations. Now, the most relevant ones are divided as follows:

(I) Compulsory Education Plan

Last time, it was scheduled to be fully realized in ten years, and it was not thought that China had 40 million out-of-school children, requiring 1.4 million teachers, 1 million classrooms, and 280 million yuan in funding each year. There was also no method for setting up schools in stages, training teachers, and increasing classrooms. This time, the program proposes to calculate all kinds of problems in a comprehensive plan in detail, and the deadline for full realization is set at 20 years.

(II) Adult Literacy Education Plan

The previous proposal to reduce illiteracy stipulated that people aged 15 to 50 must receive four months of literacy education, with people's reading books, algorithms, etc. as the subject matter, which was very simple. This time, the program plans to enable more than 202 million people to receive education in the Three Principles of the People's Thousand Character Lesson and other reading, literacy, and the use of four powers in stages within six years, train 135,000 people, and require 112,470 classrooms, requiring a total of 283.4 million yuan in funding. Moreover, it provides detailed regulations on how to train teachers, increase school buildings and equipment, budget funds, edit teaching materials, implement procedures, and compulsory methods.

(III) Teacher Training Plan

The previous proposal to reorganize the normal school system and train rural education teachers had very simple content. This time, the program specifies the completion deadline (five years), degree, term, setup method, course outline, internship method, treatment and service, secondary school teacher training method, vocational subject teacher training method, etc. in detail.

(IV) Primary Education Improvement Plan

Although there were many proposals last time, they were biased and incomplete. There were more on curriculum standards, and there were a few on teacher treatment and training, but they were all preliminary outlines. This time, the program specifies everything related to primary education in detail, such as the establishment of elementary schools and kindergartens, funding, building equipment, teachers and staff, length of study, class organization, training and education fees, curriculum, health education, and counseling system, without any omissions. In the sections on curriculum and teacher treatment, there are further methods.

(V) Secondary Education Improvement Plan

The previous proposals on secondary education were also biased and incomplete, and also

Page 12

Curriculum standards occupy the majority. This time, the program, such as the connection method between universities and elementary schools, the establishment standards of secondary schools, funding budgets, scientific experiments, the improvement of the degree of high school general subjects, the practice of vocational subjects, and the reorganization of private secondary schools, all points that the secondary education hall should pay attention to are specified in detail. Compared with the last time, it is also much more complete.

(VI) Higher Education Improvement Plan

The previous proposals on higher education, in addition to sending students abroad, holding graduation examinations, and awarding degrees, almost none remained. This time, the program has methods to enrich content, promote universities, improve student levels, and seek employment opportunities for graduates, methods for sending students abroad, methods for establishing specialized schools, and funding budgets, etc. Compared with the last time, it is also much more complete.

(7) Plan to Improve Social Education

The previous proposals regarding social education were somewhat numerous, but also incomplete. This time, the key points of the plan include implementing a general outline for supplementary education in agriculture, industry, commerce, and vocational skills; establishing and promoting major social institutions; preparing special education and rehabilitation education; improving customs and promoting public entertainment; cooperative measures between social education and school education; and budget estimates, which are much more detailed.

(8) Plan to Improve and Develop Overseas Chinese Education

The previous proposals on this topic were few. This time, all the resolutions of the previous Overseas Chinese Education Conference of the Central Training Department have been fully incorporated, and many measures have been supplemented, so this plan feels very complete. Objectives, institutions (administrative, educational associations, etc.), organizational funding design matters, school education, and social education all have detailed measures. The entire plan for overseas Chinese education is almost comprehensive.

(9) Plan to Implement Mongolian and Tibetan Education

The previous proposals on this topic were the fewest, only two, and they were both very general. This time, there are measures for administration, general education, higher education, and social education, as well as budget estimates, and compilation of libraries, etc., almost all of which are specially added, and all are very substantial.

(10) General Budget

The last time there was none at all, this time it is specially added. Because this time it is a complete plan, the total budget for the next twenty years should be included. It is estimated that more than 70 million is needed in the first year, and then 20 million is added each year, up to more than 490 million in the twentieth year. All education funds are included. After reading the above, you can know the differences between the two meetings, but this does not mean that the two meetings have any advantages or disadvantages. It's just that the last meeting seemed to be a preliminary creation, and this meeting seems to be a modification. Since there was the last meeting, there should be this meeting. Since the last meeting was like that, this meeting should be like this. They are exactly opposite and complement each other.

Finally, it should be explained that the proposals of this meeting are most lacking in two points: first, there is a lack of further implementation plans for the Three Principles of the People education; second, matters related to educational administration, such as administrative organization and administrative staff training, are almost non-existent, but it is said that there are remedial measures. Regarding administration, the Ministry of Education intends to convene the heads of education departments in each province, the heads of education bureaus in each special city (or their representatives), and their designated personnel, to hold a one- or two-day educational administration conference to specifically discuss educational administration issues and allow all members to freely propose ideas. Regarding the Three Principles of the People education, the Central Training Department intends to solicit opinions from all members in writing for reference.

As for this plan, there are naturally many shortcomings, which are not within the scope of this topic, so I won't say much now.

Summary of the Plan (1)

The Plan to Improve National Education is rich in content and more than 100,000 words long. It was very inconvenient during the conference discussion, so the reasons were removed from each plan and compiled into a summary of the plan. It was printed and distributed to all members at the meeting for discussion. The original text of the summary of each case is recorded below in installments.

▲Summary of the Preliminary Plan for Implementing Adult Supplementary Education

(1) General Outline

1. Objectives: To provide a kind of short-term school education with supplementary characteristics to the unemployed people of the country, both young and adult, and to complete literacy training within the six-year period of political tutelage.

2. Principles: (A) To enable the people to have the ability to read and write and use the four powers with the least money and the shortest period of time; (B) To start with group people first, and gradually extend to scattered people, starting from rich places and gradually extending to poor places; (C) The age of those who receive national literacy training should range from 12 to 50 years old; (D) Illiterate people have the obligation to learn, and literate people have the obligation to teach; (E) There should be very strict assessment in administration; (F) After establishing a foundation, there should be opportunities for continued progress.

3. Current Problems (A) How to enable the 320 million out-of-school people in the country to be literate and do arithmetic; (B) How to cultivate 135,000 teachers needed in six years; (C) How to increase 112,447 teaching treasures; (D) How to raise more than 283.4 million yuan in funds.

(2) Measures for Unenrolled Adults to Enter Supplementary Education and Cultivate Teachers

1. Illiterate members of small family shops and other small-scale organizations are guided by literate members living together, which is called the National Literacy Office. The nearby elementary school assesses the results. National Literacy Schools are set up in the army, factories, prisons, and all institutions, or in places with dozens or more illiterate people.

2. The teachers of National Literacy Schools are provided by county-level senior elementary schools, county-level normal schools, provincial normal schools, military academies, and secondary schools or above, which attach training classes for teachers to all students of each school for at least a three-week training, and recruit private school teachers for a two-month training. Both can train about 550,000 people, which is enough for rotation.

3. Teachers in the National Literacy Offices are filled by about 80 million elementary school students and literate adults, each receiving two months of training from the station schools and improved private schools.

4. The Ministry of Education establishes the Central National Literacy Instructor Training Institute, using the National Literacy Movement in the capital as a pilot and training center, recruiting students with a high school level or above, recruiting students in two phases each year, recruiting 80 to 100 students each time, graduating every six months, and sending them to various provinces after graduation for long-term guidance, and taking the responsibility for assessing grades. Every six months, each province must increase an average of three persons in charge of full-time adult supplementary education. After six years, each province can get more than 30 people.

(3) Measures to Increase School Buildings and Equipment

1. Each literacy school needs at least two rooms. In addition to those used by elementary schools concurrently, an average of 589 schools are needed in 1,915 counties across the country. Cities can use public institutions, charitable institutions, secondary schools or above, and rural towns can temporarily use pavilions or borrow tea shops. At other times, sunny days can use the open space of temple collapse. The equipment is also borrowed from the original ones. If it is an empty room, students should bring their own chairs.

2. Award private donations of houses, or donations to build school buildings, or public fundraising to build simple people's education halls or agricultural education halls.

(4) Budget Estimates and Allocation

1. The total budget is actually 339,524,000 yuan, and it needs 56,587,440 yuan per year on average for six years (a detailed budget table is attached in the plan).

2. In the distribution of funds, the central government bears 45% of the total amount, and should bear 25,464,348 yuan per year. The provincial and local governments bear 10% of the total amount, and should bear 5,658,744 yuan per year (except for the six provinces of Mongolia, Tibet, Suiyuan, Rehe, Chahar, Ningxia, Xikang, and Qinghai, if it is calculated by the remaining twenty-two provinces such as Jiangsu, each province will bear an average of about 250,000 yuan per year). The county and local governments bear the same amount as the central government each year.

The current number of counties and cities in the country is 2,000. Averaging the allocation, each county should raise an average of more than 12,500 yuan per year, but the population, financial resources, and environment of each county are different, so they cannot be the same. It can also be assumed to be 15,000 to 25,000 yuan for first-class counties, 5,000 to 15,000 yuan for second-class counties, and less than 5,000 yuan for third-class counties.

Exterior View of the Venue

(Railway Department Auditorium)

(Nanjing Guanghua Photography)

(5) Measures for Editing National Literacy Teaching Materials

1. The Ministry of Education compiled a Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Course, so that ordinary people can complete it in four months, one hour a day (the Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Course uses a mixed compilation method, with phonetic alphabet notes, and also includes common sense).

2. Based on the first book of the Thousand-Character Course, compile a People's Weekly with two-tenths of new words.

3. Based on the words in the Thousand-Character Course, compile a People's Series with two-tenths of new words.

4. The above publications are allowed to be reprinted by bookstores across the country, and the price should be extremely low.

(6) Implementation of Universal Talent Continuation

1. Each county and city organizes a National Literacy Training Committee, each district organizes a Literacy Branch, each township organizes a Literacy Congress, and each group organizes a Literacy Office (the list of candidates is detailed in the original plan).

2. Investigate the number of teachers in the district in stages, and their names. The total number and addresses of illiterate people in the district, and according to the following order: (A) The chief of each neighborhood should implement compulsory measures in the area two and a half months in advance, find out the situation and register it, and report it to the township branch; (B) The township branch should collect the reports from each neighborhood two months before the implementation of compulsory measures, register it, and report it to the district branch; (C) The district branch should collect the reports from all the affiliated townships one and a half months before the implementation of compulsory measures, register it, and report it to the county committee; (D) The county committee should collect the reports from all the affiliated districts one month before the implementation of compulsory measures, register it, and report it to the Education Department.

3. Distribute the teachers and the taught and notify them separately.

(A) One month before the implementation of compulsory measures, call the neighborhood to set up a school if there are more than 50 people to be taught, and if it is not convenient to set up a school, distribute and announce the teachers and the taught one by one according to the standard of one teacher and three taught; (B) If the teachers are not enough, report to the higher-level branch for allocation; (C) Those who have the obligation to teach may be exempted from the obligation after proving special circumstances, but they must pay a teaching donation for three people; (D) If there are too many teachers in the neighborhood, they should register and report to the branch for transfer to other places; (E) Distribute the supplies and distribute them separately.

(7) Scheduled Compulsory Period and Post-Compulsory Assessment

1. On July 19, the public was notified that they must finish reading the Three Principles of the People Thousand-Character Course before the end of December 25. The second announcement was made on September 1.

2. Starting from New Year's Day in the second year, compulsory measures will be implemented in the capital's towns and villages.

3. Starting from New Year's Day in the twenty-first year, compulsory measures will be implemented in the provincial capitals' towns and villages.

4. Starting from New Year's Day in the twenty-third year, compulsory measures will be implemented in the towns and villages of first-class and second-class counties.

5. Starting from New Year's Day in the twenty-fourth year, compulsory measures will be implemented in the towns and villages of third-class counties.

6. At the end of December 25, the preliminary plan will come to an end.

7. However, those places with sufficient funds and easy preparation may handle it in advance. Those with special circumstances (such as disaster areas) must not exceed the time limit unless approved.

(8) Strict Assessment Methods After Implementation

(A) Starting from New Year's Day in the twenty-sixth year, all agencies, schools, groups, factories, and shops are not allowed to hire illiterate people over the age of sixteen; (B) Those who have special circumstances and cannot receive literacy training after the compulsory order is issued can declare and approve a valid period of no more than four months; (C) After the four-month study period expires, the teacher shall report to the neighborhood office and report to the higher-level branch. Those who pass the examination will be given a literacy national certificate and an award certificate to the teacher, and their obligations will be lifted at the same time; (D) Those who fail the examination must still ask the original teacher to be responsible for teaching; (E) During the compulsory period, the county education bureau will send personnel to conduct spot checks and guidance at any time; (F) One year after the compulsory order is issued, the central government will send personnel to the provinces, the provinces will send personnel to the counties, the counties will send personnel to the districts, and the districts will send personnel to the townships to the neighborhoods to the neighbors for random tests. Those who reach 90% of the right, the person in charge and the person in charge of joint liability will be recorded as a major merit once. Those who reach 80% will be recorded as a merit once. Those who do not reach 70% will be recorded as a demerit once. Those who do not reach 60% will be recorded as a major demerit once. Those who do not reach 50% will be dismissed.

▲Summary of the Preliminary Plan for Implementing Compulsory Education

(1) Objectives

1. To enable all school-age children (40 million out-of-school children) in the country to receive four years of compulsory education.

2. Poor children can vary or shorten the period of schooling, and make up for the compulsory education they should receive through supplementary education or self-study system (details are attached to the original plan).

(2) Time Limit

1. To complete the national teacher training institutions within five years, and at the same time open 1,500 compulsory education experimental areas in cities and villages.

2. Gradually promote it later, and implement four years of compulsory education nationwide by the end of the twentieth year.

(3) Current Problems

1. How to enable all 40 million out-of-school children across the country to enroll in school within 20 years.

2. How to increase 1.4 million teachers within 20 years.

3. How to increase 1 million classrooms and 1 million sets of classroom equipment.

4. How to raise 280 million yuan of funds per year (the funds for building classrooms and cultivating teachers are not included).

(4) Measures for Training Teachers and Enrolling Children in Stages

1. About 200,000 elementary school teachers are needed in cities, and the existing secondary teacher training institutions in cities are responsible for training. About 1.2 million rural elementary school teachers are needed, and 1,500 rural normal schools will be established in counties across the country within five years, which are responsible for training. On average, each school will train 800 people. Starting from the sixth year, each school should have an average of 53 graduates per year.

2. The teachers of urban normal schools are responsible for training by the existing normal universities or major university education colleges, etc.

3. A total of 21,000 teachers are needed for rural normal schools in counties across the country, and 27 rural normal colleges and normal colleges established in various provinces are responsible for training. From the second to the fourth year, each province and each school must train 180 people.

4. The teachers of provincial rural normal colleges and specialized colleges need 540 people, and the National Compulsory Education College is responsible for training them in two years, training 270 people each year, and then continuing to train 100 people each year to fill vacancies.

5. The National Compulsory Education College and the experimental area will be established in the first year, with two experimental areas, one city and one village, for students to experiment and serve as the foundation for promoting compulsory education throughout the country.

6. The provincial rural normal college, the rural normal junior college, and the provincial compulsory education experimental area should be opened at the beginning of the second year, and there should also be two experimental areas in urban and rural areas.

7. The county rural normal school will be opened in three phases, the first three years, the fourth year, and the fifth year, each establishing one-third, and from the third to the fifth year, the country will add 500 schools per year, and 500 experimental areas in cities and villages.

Note: For details on the level of the above three normal school students, see the Summary of the Plan for Establishing Training Institutions for Teachers at All Levels and of All Kinds.

8. Starting from the sixth year, the net increase of 75,000 teachers per year can increase 75,000 elementary schools and teach 3 million children. By the eighteenth year, elementary schools will be universally established throughout the country, and compulsory education will be fully implemented in the twentieth year.

9. In addition to training teachers, the following matters will be handled: A. Register all normal school graduates in the province and order them to fill elementary school teachers; B. Strictly implement the service regulations for normal school graduates, and must order them to serve for two to five years; C. Examine non-formally graduated elementary school teachers; D. Train unqualified teachers for one or two years;

E. Examine private school teachers. Those who pass the examination will be allowed to fill elementary school teachers. Those who fail the examination will be sent to the county teacher to make up for one or two years.

(5) Measures to Increase Classrooms

(1) Use ancestral temples of the people across the country; (2) Use Confucian temples, academies, and public places; (3) Use all temples and monasteries; (4) Award private donations of houses or donations to build school buildings; (5) Public construction of extremely economical and durable school buildings.

(6) Budget Estimate

(1) The total expenditure for 20 years is 3,966,430,000 yuan (detailed plan).

(2) The central government, provinces, cities, and counties share the compulsory education expenses. Assuming that the central government and the provinces each share half in the second year, starting from the third year, the central government bears 45%, the provinces bear 10%, and the local governments bear 45%.

(3) Encourage private schools to reduce the local burden.

Talk by Mei Zhengyuan, Representative of the Hanshi Education Bureau Director

▲Describing the Number of Schools in Hanshi

Mei Zhengyuan, the representative of the Director of the Hankou Special City Education Bureau, told reporters that the Hankou Special City Education Bureau was established on July 1 last year, and it has not been long since then, so there are no educational achievements to speak of, which is very regrettable. At this conference, Director Wang Yiqun originally intended to attend in person, but because he also served as the Minister of Organization of the Municipal Party Department, and had to actively plan the future progress of municipal education, he could not come to Beijing in person. The education funds of Hanshi are currently 50,000 yuan per month (the administrative expenses of more than 9,700 yuan per month are outside the 50,000 yuan). After the summer vacation this year, it has been decided to increase to 100,000 yuan. The funds are issued monthly, and there has never been a case of arrears. There are 39 municipal primary schools and 9 senior primary schools in the city, including 3 complete primary schools, all with attached kindergartens. There are 22 registered private primary schools, and there are more than 180 private schools that have been registered. There is one municipal vocational school, with three departments: applied chemistry, dyeing and weaving, and commerce. There is one women's vocational supplementary school, with three departments: sewing, dyeing and weaving, and embroidery. There is one public education teacher training institute, which is set up to train teachers for public schools. There are 22 workers' schools, which teach workers' children during the day and workers' supplementary lessons in vocational skills in the evening. In addition, there are 7 public education centers and 3 popular libraries. After the summer vacation, it is planned to add one complete secondary school for boys and girls, both with senior high school normal departments. The Education Bureau is working hard to expand education in Hancheng. After the summer vacation, 300,000 yuan of municipal public bonds will be allocated for the construction of primary school buildings. It is planned to build 30 primary schools, each with eight grades. Among the nine complete primary schools, it is planned to convert two schools into experimental primary schools. Vocational supplementary schools will be increased by 10 schools each year, so that primary school graduates who are unable to continue their studies will be given sufficient preparation in their careers. The minimum monthly salary for primary school teachers in Hanshi is 46 yuan, and 5 yuan is added each year to 230 yuan. The minimum salary for senior primary school education is 70 yuan, and 10 yuan is added each year after three years to 140 yuan. The monthly salary of junior high school teachers is still calculated by the hour, 7 yuan per 7 hours, and 10 yuan per hour in senior high school. After three years, the monthly increase is 10 yuan, up to 180 yuan.

Talk by Lu Yougang, Director of the Guangzhou Education Bureau

▲Education is gradually progressing

Lu Yougang, Director of the Guangzhou Special Education Bureau, departed from Guangdong on the 8th and arrived in Shanghai at the same time as the three experts of the conference, Zhuang Zexuan and Zhong Rongguang. Zhuang and Zhong stayed in Shanghai for a few days, and he arrived in Beijing on the 13th. The reporter interviewed him at the hotel and made the following conversation.

The Guangzhou Education Bureau was established in the 9th year of the Republic of China. In January of this year, Guangzhou was ordered to be changed to a special city, and the Special City Education Bureau was established in March of the same year. He served as the Director. The city's education was affected by military and communist control two or three years ago, and it was not easy to maintain the status quo. There was no possibility of development. In the past one or two years, the municipal administration has been stable, and everything has gradually gotten on track. Education has been gradually progressing, and education funds have also increased the most in the past one or two years. The city's education funds have now increased to 120,000 yuan per month. There are a total of nine municipal secondary schools, including one each for middle school, teachers' college, vocational school, workers' school, commercial school, industrial school, art school, and nanny school. Two new secondary schools will be established after the summer vacation, and their school buildings are under construction. There are a total of 80 complete primary schools in the city, and more than 10 schools have attached kindergartens. Based on his personal experience, the number of primary schools should be small, and the number of grades in each school should be large, which is easier to handle and the results are easier to see. There are also nearly 30 subsidized private primary schools in the city. For detailed statistics, he has compiled a report to the conference, which will compile the recent educational overview statistics of the city separately for reference. The lowest-level assistant teacher's monthly salary for primary school teachers is 40 yuan, and the formal teacher's salary is 47 yuan and 1 jiao, which increases by 7 yuan and 5 jiao each year up to a maximum of 180 yuan. The monthly salary of middle school teachers is calculated by the hour, ranging from 5 yuan to 7 yuan for junior high school teaching, and from 8 yuan to 9 yuan for senior high school. The above are all calculated in haoyang.

Ms. Gao Junshan is an expert member of the First National Education Conference. Last year, she was sent by the Fujian Education Department to study education at the University of Michigan in the United States. She has rich knowledge and experience. Recently, she sent an educational opinion letter from the United States. The plan is well-thought-out and insightful. ▲Discussion on the Public Education Curriculum

▲Temporary Remedial Measures Before Universal Compulsory Education Can Be Realized (Three Types)

Implementing compulsory education and forced education is like talking on paper. It has been many years. Its biggest reason is the problem of funding. Judging from the current financial situation, although the government is determined to implement universal compulsory education, I am afraid that it will be difficult to realize it in the next few years. If we wait until the national financial resources are abundant before it can be implemented, this kind of ideal will forever become an illusion in our minds. But under the current economic capacity, isn't there a specific way to get close to, assuming that it cannot be fully achieved, this kind of ideal? Now, for the purpose of immediate relief, I will not hesitate to propose three methods for the reference of those who run compulsory education, but since they are neither "existing since ancient times" nor "common in Europe and the United States," I am afraid that they will inevitably be criticized by the general public in society.

(A) Compulsory Education Experimental Area Plan to Raise the Age of Enrollment and Shorten the Length of Schooling

(1) Reasons

(1) According to the preliminary plan for the implementation of compulsory education recently announced by the Ministry of Education, the length of schooling is set between the ages of 6 and 11 or 12 (school-age children) for four years. This new regulation has already been reduced by two years compared with the past, but judging from the current economic situation in our country, I am afraid that four years of compulsory education will still be difficult, so we should think of a more economical way, that is, to raise the age of enrollment from 11 to 17 years old and shorten the length of schooling for two years as a temporary relief. In this way, the national burden can be reduced by half. For four years of compulsory education, assuming that each child should cost 28 yuan, it can be reduced to 14 yuan.

(2) According to recent studies by psychological experts on adult learning, we know that the childhood period that was previously recognized as the golden age of learning is not absolute. It turns out that the learning ability of older people (those under 50) is not only not weaker than that of younger people, but sometimes even stronger than them. For materials that require reasoning ability, of course, older people are better than young children, and those who do not know how to learn and engage in muscular activities are also better than children under ten years old. Therefore, it can be inferred that children between the ages of 11 and 17, if given two years of education, may gain more basic knowledge and skills than four years of education between the ages of 6 and 12.

(3) Learning ability is not the only element of success in school. In addition, the influence of emotions is also very important. Slightly older children have a little awareness of the meaning of life. They know that if they don't

Interior of the Venue

(Nanjing Guanghua Photography)

learn, they will suffer, so they must be more diligent than young children. Their vision is also a little broader, and they can see what kind of assistance the education they receive will provide in their lives. Therefore, their learning has motivation. Therefore, the basic knowledge and skills that should be learned in four years can definitely be completed within a year if they are allocated and taught using ideal methods, and there will be better results.

(2) Measures

(1) The Ministry of Education should issue a circular to various provinces, selecting one or two counties as pilot areas for compulsory education, raising the age of enrollment, and shortening the length of schooling.

(2) Investigate the total number of children aged eleven to seventeen in the area. Children aged eleven to seventeen who are already in regular primary and secondary schools are not within the scope of the pilot project, so their numbers should be deducted.

(3) Establish a number of primary schools in the pilot area according to the needs of children aged eleven to seventeen.

(4) Compel children aged eleven to seventeen in the pilot area who are out of school to enroll in the newly established primary schools. No one may evade this under any pretext.

(5) The Ministry of Education should hire experts to develop a two-year primary school curriculum and compile textbooks for each subject, ensuring that they suit the abilities and interests of children of this age group. It should also formulate ideal teaching methods and administration to serve as a guide for implementation in each pilot area. However, all regulations should be lenient, allowing each pilot area to freely experiment according to local conditions.

(6) The progress and difficulties of the experiment in each area should be reported at any time to provide a basis for expert research and improvement.

(7) If, after two years, the results are as we expect, saving half the cost and achieving equivalent or better results, this method can be universally adopted in various regions. When the national finances are sufficient, the duration of universal compulsory education can be increased to three, four, six, or eight years.

(B) Proposal for a Self-Study System Pilot Project

(1) Rationale

At a time when there is a shortage of teachers and school buildings, universal compulsory education is impossible. The most pitiful thing is that every year when school starts, many children who come to enroll are turned away because the quotas in each class are full. (Moreover, this happens even in some very expensive private schools.) Everyone fulfills the obligation of paying taxes, but does not equally enjoy the right to willingly pay extra. This is very unfair. Therefore, we have no choice but to seek a second-best solution and adopt a self-study system. With this system, there is no need to increase teachers, school buildings, or equipment, and out-of-school children or adults can learn some basic knowledge and skills.

(2) Measures

(1) Each province should designate several counties as areas for piloting a self-study system.

(2) Designate several primary schools in a county, located in convenient places, as centers for the self-study system. People who want to attend school but cannot, or who cannot attend full-day classes (regardless of whether they are adults or children), can come to the school to receive several self-study instructions, and then take the materials home to study on their own.

(3) The Ministry of Education should hire experts to determine the steps for self-study, curriculum standards, and textbook content.

(4) The Ministry of Education should compile self-study textbooks for adults and children for use.

(5) After a certain period of self-study, those who pass the exam can be issued a certain certificate.

(6) Each school should report the results of the self-study system pilot project for research and improvement.

(7) If good results are obtained, it can be promoted and implemented (To be continued in Important News)

National Scout Review News

▲ General Review Begins on the 16th

Nanjing Telegram: The General Review of the Boy Scouts of China is scheduled to begin on the 16th, with camping at Xiaoying Review Ground. As of this report, there are scouts from five places, including four provinces (Hunan, Jiangxi, Anhui, Hubei, Shandong) and Shanghai Special Municipality, totaling over 900 people, including over a hundred girl scouts. Due to the rain, the camping ground has not yet been completely prepared. The reception department of the organizing committee is arranging for them to stay temporarily at the Public Theater, the May 30th Middle School, and other places.

▲ Number of Registered Troops Yesterday

Nanjing Telegram: The Boy Scout Training Department began registering Boy Scout troops from various regions. As of the 14th, a total of 197 troops had been registered as qualified, with 13,333 Boy Scouts and 1,118 service personnel nationwide.

▲ All Free for Boat and Ship Travel

The Ministry of Transportation has ordered all shipping companies to comply with the first National Boy Scout General Review and Grand Jamboree, scheduled to be held in Beijing on the 18th of this month. The headquarters has sent personnel to discuss the matter with the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Transportation. The Ministry of Transportation has agreed to provide complete free passage on ships. The ministry, in order to be cautious, has formulated free passage measures and various certificates, specifying the measures in detail to prevent abuses. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and other commercial shipping companies in this city received the ministry's order yesterday, along with a simple guide to free passage measures and three types of free passage certificates (A, B, and C), instructing them to comply.

▲ Jimei Naval and Land Scouts Arrive in Shanghai

Going to Beijing on the 16th to Participate in the General Review

The Fujian Jimei School's highly reputable Naval and Land Scout troops have sent a portion of their members as representatives to attend this first National Boy Scout General Review. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday, consisting of two naval scout troops and four land scout troops, totaling sixty people, led by the troop commander and deputy commander, Gu Zheng and Leng Xueqiao, and instructors including Chen Meiqing, Wu Risheng, and Lin Yunlai. They are camping at the Municipal Public Sports Field. At 10 a.m., they lined up to pay their respects to Chen Dezheng, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, who also gave a welcoming speech, expressing great appreciation.

▲ Jinan University Scouts Set Off

The Boy Scout troop of National Jinan University, directly under the 64th Regiment, left for Beijing yesterday to participate in the first National General Review and Grand Jamboree.

▲ Guangda Scouts Come to Shanghai

The Boy Scout troop of the Guangzhou National Sun Yat-sen University Affiliated Middle School sent Luo Fu team members He Shiyu and Jiang Zhenhong as representatives to attend this National Boy Scout General Review. They arrived in Shanghai yesterday and are scheduled to take a train to Beijing today.

▲ Patriotic Girls' School Scouts Depart Early for Beijing

Since the founding of the Party Scout Corps the year before last, the Patriotic Girls' School in this city immediately established the 7th Regiment and actively trained them. Last year, they held joint jamborees in Hangzhou and Shanghai successively. The regiment has extensive experience in marching techniques, and their spirit of service is also relentless, not inferior to men despite being women. This time, the capital is holding a national Boy Scout grand review, and the regiment is even more eager to participate. They departed on the night train yesterday, with approximately a hundred members carrying luggage, led by the regimental commander Huang Shan and instructor Wang Xiying, who led the troops to the station in an orderly fashion. It is reported that the regiment has senior students from the physical education department, who plan to visit along the way after their graduation review during the summer vacation.

Record of the Second Day of the Jiangsu Scouts Jamboree

▲ Instructors Sworn In

▲ Closing Ceremony Today

Nearly a thousand Boy Scouts from Jiangsu Province came to the provincial capital to participate in the Grand Jamboree. Due to inclement weather, the first day of the event was met with heavy rain. The competition was halted after the opening ceremony. However, the overall spirit was full, and the organizers were particularly enthusiastic. Yesterday (the 14th) morning, despite the torrential rain, they still held morning exercises and camp inspections. At 8 a.m., a memorial week for the late Premier was held, with Chen Bangxi, the camp director, reporting on party affairs and the general political situation. He continued, saying that the halt of this Grand Jamboree due to rain was unfortunate. Due to the cold weather, most of the young children were lightly clothed, and it was feared that their bodies would not be able to withstand it. It was decided to dismantle the camp at 12 noon on the 14th. If the weather cleared on the 15th, an awards ceremony would be held. On the 16th, they would go to Beijing. Yesterday, after twelve o'clock, all the tents in the public sports field were removed and they are now stationed in the provincial and county party headquarters and various primary schools in the urban area.

▲ Instructors Sworn in

The Jiangsu Provincial Boy Scout Instructors held a swearing-in ceremony at the Provincial Party Headquarters conference room yesterday (the 14th) afternoon at 4 p.m. The details are recorded below.

You all have a long history with the Boy Scouts, and good results. The swearing-in ceremony is generally regarded as a routine matter. However, your swearing-in today should not be treated as routine. It should be known that after this swearing-in, all of you will bear a much heavier responsibility. In the current situation of Chinese society, the general public has not fully recognized the Boy Scouts. The responsibility of making the public understand the Boy Scouts belongs to you. At the same time, the instructors who are appointed according to the Boy Scout service regulations are quite clear about the ideology and are also party members. Therefore, your responsibilities seem to be twofold. I deeply hope that you will promote Chinese society with the spirit of the Boy Scouts, and on the party's side, work hard for the party with the spirit of the Boy Scouts. Therefore, your swearing-in is more important than other swearing-in ceremonies. You have good experience and a clear understanding of the party, and you will definitely be able to bear this responsibility. Jiangsu's Boy Scouts can be called advanced in the country. Judging from the results of this Grand Jamboree, it is expected that there will be even better results in the future when participating in the National General Review. I hope that you will continue to work hard and develop Jiangsu's Boy Scouts as a model for the whole country.

▲Results of Last Night's Judging

Local News

China and Japan's Tariffs Must Be Equal and Reciprocal

▲Three National Goods Groups Send Telegram to the Government

The China National Goods Maintenance Association and other groups request that goods such as Chinese silk be included in the Sino-Japanese treaty for reciprocity. They sent a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, which reads: (abbreviated title) On the 4th of this month, newspapers in Shanghai published a Nanjing telegram from the Asahi Shimbun of Japan stating that there are 62 items, totaling 101 types, in the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty's provisions for reciprocal treatment of Japanese goods shipped to China, which still follow the current import tariff names and do not use the name of reciprocity. There is no mention of the shipment of national goods to Japan and Korea. It has been found that unequal treaties in the past were harmful in that there were only tariff regulations for Japanese goods shipped to China, but no tariff regulations for Chinese goods shipped to Japan. As a result, Chinese goods to Japan were subject to harsh levies, and our country could not interfere, causing a major disaster. There is no reason to repeat the same mistakes and seek self-destruction this time. All colleagues in the Chinese goods industry are extremely panicked upon reading this. Abolishing unequal treaties is the most important instruction of our late Premier. The relationship between China and Japan is the closest, and our country has suffered the most from the unequal Sino-Japanese treaties. Now, when we are revising the commercial treaty, it is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. All the unequal points of the past should be changed to equality. As for reciprocal tariff rates, both parties should have equal tariffs on the same type of goods, such as raw materials and raw materials, and finished products and finished products, before reciprocity can be achieved. Now, regarding the issue of reciprocal agreements in the Sino-Japanese Commercial Treaty, our side firmly declares that there is no such thing, while Japan openly announces it. Judging from this, Japanese goods shipped to China can get reciprocity for as many as 101 types, but whether Chinese goods shipped to Japan can get reciprocity, and what goods and tariff rates are involved, is unclear. For example, in the past, from the Qing Dynasty to the eighth year of the Republic of China, Chinese silk shipped to Japan and Korea was subject to a 7.5% ad valorem duty. At that time, Chinese silk was sold in large quantities. Since the ninth year of the Republic of China, it has been changed to a tax of 520 yuan per 100 catties, and at that time, sales had already been reduced by half. Unexpectedly, since the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, it has been changed to 100% of the estimated value, and the estimated value has been arbitrarily increased. Since then, sales of Chinese silk have been completely cut off, and it has been six years since then. The silk industry has suffered heavy losses. As for ramie cloth, from the Qing Dynasty to the eighth year of the Republic of China, it was subject to a 7.5% ad valorem duty. Since the ninth year of the Republic of China, it was suddenly changed to a specific duty of 10 yuan to 56 yuan per 100 catties. Since the thirteenth year of the Republic of China, it was again changed to 12 yuan to 80 yuan per 100 catties. Such heavy import taxes have led to sluggish sales, which have decreased year by year. This association believes that the key to the shipment of Chinese goods to Japan and Korea is at this time, which is extremely important to the national economy and people's livelihood. Therefore, we boldly risk offending and submit this telegraph jointly. We humbly request that Your Excellencies insist on mutual tariff autonomy. If reciprocity is agreed upon, please approve the inclusion of goods that are commonly sold to Japan and Korea, such as Chinese silk, ramie cloth, porcelain, and southern goods, in the reciprocity list, so as to conform to the principle of equality and maintain the livelihood of industry and commerce. If the Japanese side does not agree, our side must not sign the agreement. The telegraph does not overcome the urgency of the matter, awaiting orders. Sincerely, the China National Goods Maintenance Association, the Shandong Fellow Townsmen Association in Shanghai, and the Shanghai Ramie Cloth Association. (Signature)

Examination of Sino-Japanese Tariff Agreement Obtained by Japanese Consulate

▲ Privy Council of Japan Scheduled to Meet on the 17th

The draft of the Sino-Japanese tariff agreement was brought back to Japan by Yokotake, a commercial official of the Japanese Embassy, for submission to the Japanese government for review. It has been several days since then. According to news from the Japanese Embassy Office yesterday, the draft was once reviewed by the Privy Council's Review Committee the day before yesterday (the 12th). It is now scheduled to convene a second review meeting on the 17th of this month. Once it passes the third reading, it can be formally approved. At that time, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs will instruct Ambassador Shigemitsu to go to Beijing on a scheduled date to sign the official agreement. Commercial Official Yokotake will also be ordered to return to China, it is said.

Unanimous Opposition to Japanese Warships Conducting Large-Scale Exercises in Chinese Territory

▲ Declaration by the Ninth District Party Headquarters: The facts of Japanese imperialism's aggression against our country are deeply imprinted in our minds. Examples include carving up Korea, seizing Taiwan, occupying Lushun and Dalian, invading Manchuria and Mongolia, coercing treaties, and creating tragic incidents. Tracing back their intentions, they will not be satisfied until they devour China entirely. Recently, taking advantage of our central government's large-scale campaign to suppress rebels, they have spared no effort to violate international law, dispatching large numbers of Japanese warships to China to conduct reconnaissance and demonstration operations. Eventually, due to the unyielding spirit of our people, they aroused nationwide opposition. Instead of realizing the danger and withdrawing promptly, they have intensified their actions, even attempting to gather minesweeping squadrons to conduct large-scale exercises on Zhoushan Island in our territory. Upon hearing this shocking news, this committee is deeply indignant. We believe that this is a disregard for our national sovereignty and an insult to our national identity. We cannot bear to sit idly by and remain silent. In addition to submitting a request to the government authorities for serious negotiations, and leading all party members in the district to pledge our support and face any danger without hesitation, we also hope that all compatriots across the country will rise up together and engage in further struggles with these Japanese imperialists to protect our national rights and avenge our humiliation. This declaration is hereby made, please be aware.
