Rice Price Limits Must Not Be Violated

▲ Rice Merchants Who Violated Price Limits Issue Pledges to Close the Case

▲ Rice Merchants Who Instigated Rice Boats Not to Sell Are Summoned for Admonishment

Since the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau imposed limits on rice prices, there has been a gradual downward trend. However, the bureau recently received confidential reports that some unscrupulous merchants are still secretly engaging in acts of sabotage. On Sunday, the bureau sent personnel to cooperate with Section Member Zhang of the Public Security Bureau to conduct investigations and summoned He Yongxiang and other rice merchants who violated price limits to the case. They should have been detained, but the rice merchants repeatedly pleaded for exemption from punishment, promising not to violate the limits again. Considering that they were first-time offenders, they were ordered to have the white rice they had loaded re-evaluated and priced at 19.5 yuan per picul for sale, and they issued a pledge to close the case. The rice shops that helped sell the rice were also given severe warnings and issued pledges. If there are any further violations, they will be punished according to the police regulations, with a five-day detention. Furthermore, Lu, a merchant who sells Changbang rice, was found to have instigated Changbang rice boats not to sell. He was summoned by the Public Security Bureau to the Social Affairs Bureau for a stern admonishment and ordered to clear the source and not to disobey government orders again, lest he be prosecuted.

Change of Subsidy for Grain Regulation

▲ Period: From June to the End of July This Year

▲ Municipal Government Orders the Finance and Social Affairs Bureaus to Discuss and Decide

The original Shanghai Public Funds and Public Property Management Committee previously received a letter from the original Fund and Property Management Office, stating that in December of the 18th year of the Republic, it was instructed by the County Government to prepare for grain regulation. It immediately convened a meeting of district chiefs to discuss and decide. The meeting decided that the period for grain regulation would be from June to the end of July of the 19th year of the Republic. The funds for grain regulation, about 9,000 yuan from accumulated interest, would be used. The method of grain regulation would be for each district to first investigate the extremely poor and the next-to-poor, create separate lists, and then calculate and distribute accordingly. This was immediately reported to the County Government for approval. Furthermore, in February of this year, a joint meeting of the accounting officer of the office and the district chiefs decided to follow the old rules of the 9th year of the Republic and distribute money instead of grain, subsidizing the price of rice for the extremely poor and the next-to-poor separately. However, in the 9th year of the Republic, 25,000 yuan was spent on grain subsidies, which was distributed to various cities and counties according to the amount of land tax. The list for the 19th year shows that the eight townships under the county should receive a total of over 9,100 yuan, and the eleven townships incorporated into the Special Municipality should receive a total of over 15,800 yuan. The grain subsidies for the districts under the county would be distributed starting on June 1st, so the office's distribution of funds would also be distributed at the same time to areas suffering from hardship. This was resolved by the 31st standing meeting of the committee, which decided to amend the names of the districts in the region according to the current system and submit them to the Municipal Government for review. After receiving the report, the Municipal Government, regarding the method of distribution and payment for the eleven cities and counties, specially instructed the Social Affairs and Finance Bureaus to discuss and decide and report back in detail for consideration.

Chinese Staff Member of Customs Promoted to Customs Commissioner

Since the Ministry of Finance's Customs Administration appointed Meierhe as the Inspector General of Customs, Meierhe, in view of China's determination to recover customs administration, has made every effort to promote its improvement, and to improve the treatment of Chinese staff members, so that Chinese and foreign staff members are in an equal position, as an initial step towards Chinese autonomy, especially in the measures taken. This time, he has specially promoted three Chinese staff members to the position of Customs Commissioner, namely He Zhihui, the Customs Commissioner of Hangzhou Customs, Weng Junshouzhen of Yangzhou Customs, and Ding Juitang of the Inspector General of Customs Office. Mr. Ding is an early graduate of the Beijing Customs School, with excellent academic knowledge and capable handling of affairs. He is known to the Customs Commissioner and the Inspector General of Customs. Two years ago, he was promoted to Chief Secretary of Chinese Affairs, acting as Customs Commissioner. Now, he has been officially awarded the responsibility of Customs Commissioner. Counting Mr. He, Mr. Weng, and Mr. Ding, after their promotion to Customs Commissioner, there are still Zhou Junziheng, the Customs Commissioner of Chongqing Customs, holding this position, making a total of four people. Those who are currently acting as Customs Commissioners include Zhang Junbolie of Wenzhou Customs and Qiao Junruyong of Yuezhou Customs. Mr. Zhang and Mr. Qiao are also graduates of the Beijing Customs School. Furthermore, since the five external regular customs offices of Yangzhou, Fengyang, and other customs offices, as well as Wenzhou, Wuhu, and other ports, have been managed by the Customs on behalf of them, the tax revenue has more than doubled compared to before. Song Ziwen, the Minister of Finance, has repeatedly praised the customs officers' ability to handle affairs and their integrity, it is said.

Reorganization of Two Railways Is Not a Reduction of Staff

The staff and employees of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Ningbo Railways have recently undergone a reorganization due to the unified organization of the Ministry of Railways. As a result, the compilation and transportation sections of the two railways have been abolished first. The division chiefs and clerks of various departments are all in a state of panic. Therefore, yesterday afternoon, they elected representatives to petition Director Liu of the two railways to protect the employees. Director Liu explained to the representatives that this reorganization is not a reduction of staff, and that those who have already been laid off are being taken care of, and he guaranteed that there would be no reduction of staff. Employee benefits are also guaranteed. The representatives were very satisfied with Director Liu's frankness and have informed their colleagues of this intention. It is thought that the staff and employees of the two railways will be able to serve with peace of mind upon hearing this news. This is also good news for the transportation sector.

Merger of China Merchants Bureau Shanghai Branch Implemented Yesterday

▲ Deputy Section Chief Li Yunliang Has Returned to Shanghai

The news that the Shanghai branch of the China Merchants Bureau has been merged into the business section of the head office, with Bureau Chief Shen Zhongyi renamed as Section Chief, and former Deputy Section Chief of the Business Section Li Yunliang continuing to hold his original position, etc., has already been reported in previous newspapers. It is now learned that the merger of the bureau was implemented yesterday (Monday). A part of the business section of the head office also moved to the inner entrance downstairs (formerly the front desk) to work yesterday. The organization of the section will follow the new system, dividing into five units: navigation, cargo solicitation, branch offices, auditing, and disaster relief. If there are any unsuitable aspects, they can be changed at any time. The head of the section, Zhao, has stipulated that the number of staff in the section is fifty people. Because the Shanghai branch, together with the business section of the head office, has more than one hundred people, which is twice the current stipulated number, there is no way to accommodate them. Therefore, Section Chief Shen is currently discussing accommodation methods with Zhao. It is said that the extra personnel will be selected for their competence and assigned to branch offices to work, or to serve as inspectors, or they will be laid off. No decision has been made yet, so the staff of the section has not been announced.

Li Yunliang, the deputy section chief who was previously dispatched to inspect the Yangtze River area, returned to Shanghai yesterday morning. When Mr. Li arrived in Hankou, the bureau's Yangtze River ships were requisitioned. After strenuous negotiations, they were released. The purpose of Mr. Li's trip was to inspect the branch offices and contact Hakka businessmen in the Xunhan area. Now that the matter has been completed, he took the Jianghua ship to Beijing, changed to a train, and returned to Shanghai, arriving yesterday morning. It is said that Mr. Li's contact with Hakka businessmen in Xunhan and other ports was very harmonious, and he has many plans for the branch offices. The bureau's Yangtze River route business will have new developments in the future.

Huang Boqiao to Sail Abroad Tomorrow

The three special municipalities of Beijing, Hankou, and Shanghai have jointly recommended Huang Boqiao, the director of the Shanghai Public Affairs Bureau, to attend the Second World Power Conference in Germany. It is now learned that Mr. Huang has completed all preparations and is scheduled to sail abroad tomorrow (the 16th) on the Great Lakes Company's Café Olé ship. Those who have even slight friendship with Mr. Huang have been hosting banquets to send him off, boosting his morale. After Mr. Huang sets sail, the bureau affairs he leaves behind will be handled by the bureau's secretary, Xu Yuanfang, as instructed by Mayor Zhang.

Yunnan Fellow Countrymen Host Farewell Banquet for Zhang Weihan

▲ Zhang Has Postponed His Departure to Around the 20th

▲ If There Is No Definite News of the French Envoy Coming South, He Will Leave Shanghai

Yunnanese from all walks of life in Shanghai held a public farewell banquet for Zhang Weihan, the representative of the province for treaty revision and the newly appointed Director of Civil Affairs of Yunnan, at the Fawang Palace Garden Hotel yesterday. Although it was only a simple tea party, more than one hundred fellow countrymen from Yunnan attended, making it quite a grand occasion. The following is a record:

▲ Arrangement of the Venue: The venue was the hotel's main hall. Outside the venue, a banner was hung, reading "Yunnanese Fellow Countrymen in Shanghai Respectfully Send Off Mr. Zhang Chunou." Inside the venue, more than thirty seats were arranged, with four people seated around each seat. Mr. Zhang and the temporary chairman Zhang Yaozeng were seated opposite each other, creating a solemn atmosphere.

▲ Chairman's Speech: Briefly stated, "Mr. Zhang Chunou is an outstanding talent from our Yunnan. For more than ten years, he has served his hometown and achieved remarkable results, which are admired by the people of Yunnan. In the winter of the year before last, he represented Yunnan Province in Beijing to participate in the revision of the Sino-French Vietnam Trade Agreement, upholding his commitment to alleviate the suffering of the Yunnanese people and increase their happiness. Now, he has been urged to return by telegram from Yunnan, upholding his spirit of serving the local area and striving to build and benefit the Yunnanese people through this participation in treaty revision. We greatly admire Mr. Chunou's past achievements and have high hopes for his future plans. Therefore, we have specially held this meeting to express our farewell."

▲ Mr. Zhang's Reply: Briefly stated, "I came to Beijing to represent Yunnan Province the year before last to participate in the revision of the Sino-French Trade Agreement. Everything can be found in previous newspaper reports. The draft agreement has been drafted, but the French side is still delaying on various pretexts and has not come to Beijing to sign the agreement for a long time, causing me to stay in Shanghai for a long time, unable to return. Recently, due to repeated telegrams urging me to return from the provincial government, I will come to Shanghai again when the signing of the trade agreement is scheduled. However, this morning I received a phone call from Foreign Minister Wang, saying that there is news of the French envoy coming south to sign the agreement again, asking me to wait temporarily. However, the French envoy has repeatedly delayed, and I am not sure if he will definitely come. However, due to Foreign Minister Wang's request, I will postpone my departure to the 20th. I am ashamed and unworthy of such a grand farewell from everyone. I am even more ashamed when I hear what the chairman said just now."

▲ Mr. Zhang's Departure Date: Due to Foreign Minister Wang's request to stay, Mr. Zhang has returned the original Asian Royal Ship and will wait for news from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. If the French envoy still has no definite news of coming south around the 20th, he will leave Shanghai on the President Coolidge or President Madison to return to Yunnan.

Counterfeit Banknotes Discovered on the Market

▲ East Three Provinces Banknotes Altered to Look Like General Banknotes

According to financial sources, recently, someone has been erasing the words "East Three Provinces Bank" from the banknotes of the East Three Provinces Bank, rewriting them as banknotes of Shanghai's general banks, and using them on the market. Currently, the financial sector and the police are conducting a strict investigation. The details of the alteration of the banknotes are photographed below to facilitate attention from all sectors.

Front: The blank space above is where the words "East Three Provinces Bank" have been erased and rewritten with the name of another bank.

The original text below reads: "This note is equivalent to twelve jiaos of silver dollar, and it is generally used in the three eastern provinces and can be converted to Shanghai silver." The altered note uses a dark blue or black stamp to cover most of it. The English words "Fengtian" on both sides below have been erased and changed to the Chinese words "Shanghai."

Back: The English above is still the original text of the East Three Provinces Bank: "Provincial Bank of the Three Eastern Provinces."

The English word "Shanghai" is printed below.

Wireless Radio Station Established at Wusong Fortress

The South Shitou, North Shitou, and Shizilin Forts under the Wusong Fortress Headquarters are the first gateway to the Yangtze River and are of utmost importance in protecting the capital. Fortress Commander Deng Zhenquan, in view of the recent turbulent situation and urgent military messages, ordered all forts under his command to be on strict alert day and night. In order to facilitate the rapid transmission of military intelligence, he submitted a request to the Ministry of Military Affairs of the National Government to establish a shortwave wireless radio station at the fortress to facilitate direct communication with all parties through telephone and telegraph to strengthen defense. Yesterday, Commander Deng received instructions from the Ministry of Military Affairs for approval, and the ministry forwarded it to the Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force for the issuance of a generator, which will send personnel to Wusong to install it soon, it is said.

The Extraordinary Tragedy of Lingbao, Henan Province

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Relief Association received Xue Runzhi, the representative of the Lingbao County Disaster Relief Committee in Henan Province, and Zhang Weichen and Zhang Pinsan, the representatives of the Henan Province Disaster Victims Appeal, who personally came to the association to request relief, and they described the situation in Lingbao, which has always been a cotton-producing area, but has unfortunately suffered from continuous military and banditry disasters, followed by droughts, and has fallen into a desperate situation. Starving people are everywhere. They have been relying on the dried flowers of cotton trees, the cakes pressed from cotton seeds, or the bark, leaves, wheat tips, grain stalks, etc., to fill their stomachs, but now they have nothing left. Unfortunately, an epidemic is spreading, and the common people, with their pallid faces, are being infected at a rate of eight or nine out of ten. Even close relatives such as fathers and sons, brothers, and spouses can only watch them die and weep to the sky. It is said that the relief funds raised by the association for Henan have been successively delivered to the Kaifeng Chinese and Foreign Relief Association for distribution. All counties in Henan are suffering from disasters, and the disasters are all tragic. It can be said that it is a drop in the bucket. It is hoped that all sectors will find ways to help, so that not only Lingbao County will be grateful, it is said.

Business Consolidation Association Cables Request to Prohibit Extortion of License Fees

The Business Consolidation Association yesterday sent a telegram to the Jiangsu Finance Commissioner requesting strict prohibition of tax offices from extorting license fees. The telegram stated: On the 11th of this month, the Shanghai Chinese Grain and Bean Cake Trade Association stated in a letter that businesses such as Qian Chang & Co. purchase local goods such as grains and rapeseed in various cities and towns in western Zhejiang. They load these goods onto registered civilian boats and first pay taxes at local tax bureaus. They then sail to Jiaxing to declare customs, pay the regular and additional taxes, and carry the relevant documents to Shanghai for sale. All tax offices along the way are not allowed to re-levy taxes and must release the boats upon verification of the customs documents, without inventing new charges or extorting fees. These regulations have been firmly established. However, the various branches under the jurisdiction of the Jiangsu Five-Percent Tax Office arbitrarily extort license fees whenever merchants' registered civilian boats carrying goods pass through, charging six yuan per boat at Tagang, four yuan at Desheng, four yuan at Minhang, and even for boats traveling from Shanghai to Jiaxing. If the fees are not paid, the officials detain the boats. The boatmen claim that the Jiangsu Finance Department issued strict orders prohibiting extortion in March 1919, October 1927, and July 1929. They ask why the license fees are being charged again. The officials claim that the fees are being collected under the instruction of the office director to supplement insufficient funds. It is difficult to determine whether this is due to the director's instructions or the officials' excuses. The businesses operate grain cargo ships and cannot avoid these tax offices, resulting in significant losses due to years of extortion. In response to this, we request that your association send a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, ordering subordinates to thoroughly investigate the matter, abolish the extortion of license fees, and severely punish those who violate the law, in the interest of public service, etc. The Association notes that the practice of levying license fees at tax checkpoints has long been entrenched, and past orders prohibiting it have been mere formalities. Few have been punished, leading to increasing audacity among these individuals. The letter reports that officials are seeking personal gain, using the excuse of compensating for comparisons. They are trying to make the government a scapegoat. The businesses claim that the losses are enormous and they cannot tolerate it, requesting a thorough investigation. The Association believes that while the license fees are an unofficial practice with no receipts to prove it, there are witnesses who can be questioned. Furthermore, the extortion of fees from cargo ships is a common practice. If investigators are sent to conduct secret investigations on the ground, it would not be difficult to uncover the truth and deter others through punishment. The Association, seeing that past investigations have been mere formalities, has taken the liberty to offer its views. We hope that your office will consider the difficulties faced by businesses and secretly send dedicated and capable personnel to conduct a thorough investigation and punish those who violate the law, in order to eliminate the long-standing problem and alleviate business difficulties in the interest of public service. Respectfully, Shanghai Special Municipality Business Consolidation Committee.

Continued Report on the Rope Workers' Wage Increase Movement

Regarding the rope workers' wage increase, the workers discussed the matter yesterday. Representatives of the Party's Economic Action Group reported on the findings of their investigation into the wages of workers in various shops. They found that the wages in their industry are extremely low and the working hours are longer than in other industries. Furthermore, more than ten workers have been suspended from work for demanding a wage increase, which is due to the lack of unity in the industry. With the rising cost of living, it will be difficult to manage without a wage increase. After deliberation, it was decided that because the wages in various shops are too disparate, they will request a 30% increase based on the highest current wage to standardize wages. All working hours will be eight hours per day. They will request this increase from the shop owners and print a notice to be distributed to the shops by representatives, who will also explain the workers' difficulties and the need for a wage increase to the shop owners, requesting their prompt approval so that the workers can work with peace of mind. They will hold another meeting after receiving a response.

Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Held Talks with Representatives of Various Trade Unions Yesterday

▲ Reporting the Truth about the Hoji Strike

The Preparatory Committee of the Shanghai Special Municipality Federation of Trade Unions held a meeting with representatives of various trade unions in the city at 2:00 PM yesterday. Representatives from over 130 trade unions, including the Newspaper Delivery Workers' Union, totaling over 250 people, attended. Lu Jingshi presided over the meeting and reported on the purpose of the meeting. He also outlined the causes, course, and resolution of the Hoji strike, as well as the Communist Party's exploitation of the situation. Gu Yongquan of the Preparatory Committee further elaborated that the Hoji factory initially faced difficulties due to the large number of workers and limited egg supply, making it difficult to allocate work and maintain expenses. Later, the workers demanded that no workers be dismissed. After the Social Affairs Bureau mediated a resolution, the second and third branches signed agreements. However, a dispute arose over the first clause, which was resolved after mediation by the authorities. However, the Communist Party used this as a pretext for propaganda, causing young students to become emotionally charged and rally in support. After explanation, this did not lead to a major disturbance. However, the Communist Party members then used this as a pretext to exploit the situation in the Shanghai concession. The Federation of Trade Unions has invited you to discuss this matter, hoping that you will not listen to them, be used by them, or go astray and become unacceptable to the Party and the nation.

Housing Dispute in Zhen'an Lane Heard Yesterday

The landlord of Zhen'an Lane on Ximen Road in the French Concession gave notice to all tenants to vacate the premises by April 10. The tenants formed a joint housing association and unanimously opposed the eviction. On April 8, the landlord cut off the water supply. However, the tenants still refused to move. On April 10, the landlord commissioned lawyer Fei Xizhen to notify each tenant to vacate the premises within three days, or construction would begin. The tenants also commissioned lawyer Da Xian to respond, refusing to move. Therefore, the landlord requested the police station to send two Chinese constables to the premises with workers yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM to start construction. However, all the tenants refused. The tenants declared to the workers that the negotiations had not been resolved and requested that they temporarily stop construction, which the workers refused, resulting in a conflict between the two sides and preventing the construction from proceeding. After the landlord reported to the police station, the Songshan Road Police Station dispatched several Chinese and foreign detectives to conduct an on-site investigation. After the tenants' representatives detailed the situation, the detectives reported the situation to the head of the police station, who invited the lawyers and parties involved to the police station yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM to discuss the matter.

News from Various Trade Unions

▲ British American Tobacco Factory Union Quick Telegraph: To the esteemed members of the Qingdao Special Municipality Party Headquarters: Having read the news on the 11th, we were shocked to learn that nine workers from the Qingdao British American Tobacco Company were arrested for refusing to return to work. The workers sent representatives to your department to petition, putting forward five conditions for resuming work. Your department dispatched representatives to accompany the workers' representatives back to the factory to persuade them to resume work. The workers refused mediation, resulting in a conflict with the police, leading to the arrest of over forty male and female workers and the immediate dissolution of the Tobacco Manufacturing and Printing Unions. The Qingdao British American Tobacco Factory workers had previously raised demands for wage increases due to the rising cost of living (male workers demanded an increase of 20 cents, and female workers demanded an increase of 10 cents). With the mediation of your department and government agencies, a victory was achieved, and the labor dispute was expected to be resolved. However, after Cao Yunxiang was dispatched from the Shanghai headquarters to Qingdao, a sudden announcement was made to shut down the factory, causing thousands of British American Tobacco Factory workers in Qingdao to suddenly become unemployed under dual oppression. Our association knows that this is a tactic used by the factory to exert pressure and is not a genuine long-term shutdown. We believe that during the industrial revolution, labor-capital struggles are unavoidable. However, now workers are being arrested for refusing to return to work unconditionally, and unions are being banned for failing to resume work. We know that the arrogance of imperialist capitalists will inevitably increase, and the British American Tobacco Factory workers in Qingdao will have no way out. Our association and the Qingdao British American Tobacco Union are closely related, sharing weal and woe. We deeply feel the pain of their predicament and dare not shy away from speaking out. We urge you to release the innocent arrested workers as soon as possible, restore the unjustly banned unions, and lead the workers of the Qingdao British American Tobacco Factory to advance on the road of the Three People's Principles. This is fortunate for the labor movement and fortunate for our association. Respectfully, Shanghai British American Tobacco Factory Union.

▲ Huayang Printing Union held its citywide representative meeting on the 12th. Xu Delin presided over the meeting. The following items were discussed: (A) A small number of representatives reported that the capitalists were not fulfilling the newly agreed conditions and requested review. It was decided to submit the case to the Social Affairs Bureau one by one, summoning them to order them to fulfill the agreement. (B) Wang Yanshan reported that his son, Wang Bingchun, had worked at the Traffic Printing Bureau for many years and unfortunately died of illness without funds for the funeral. He requested the capitalists for compensation. It was decided to recommend to the capitalists to request compensation, and to raise donations from members for relief. (C) It was proposed to the Municipal Party Headquarters to establish the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions as soon as possible. The proposal was approved.

Local News Two

A Young Man Was Assassinated in Jinjiazhai Lane Yesterday Afternoon

▲ Accompanied by a woman in a secluded alley

▲ Assailant opens fire from behind

▲ Deceased was slightly plump, resembling a businessman

▲ Autopsy to be conducted by the court this morning

Yesterday around 11:30 AM, an assassination of a young man around 26 or 27 years old occurred outside the iron gate of Jinjiazhai Lane, opposite Shou Kang Soy Sauce Garden on the east side of Dashalu, Shanhai Pass Road. The deceased was shot twice and lay dead in Jinfuli, his head a bloody mess, a gruesome sight. The following is a record of the reporter's investigation, divided into sections:

▲ Jinfuli Lane: A tortuous path Jinjiazhai, located on the east side of Dashalu, Shanhai Pass Road, is a tortuous path with streets crisscrossing. Although the residents are lined up side by side, the area is extremely secluded. It connects Chenjia浜 to the east, extends to Avenue Edward VII to the south, reaches Shanhai Pass Road to the north, and connects to Dashalu to the west. Although the alley is accessible from all directions, there are very few pedestrians. Therefore, thugs who enter this area consider it a rabbit's burrow, making it easy to escape.

▲ Two Gunshots Heard at Noon Yesterday around 11:30 AM, the residents in the area, mostly middle-class people, were either having lunch or cooking when they suddenly heard two gunshots in the alley. At first, they thought it was neighbors setting off firecrackers and didn't pay attention. Later, they heard a commotion and realized something had happened. The residents of the alley all rushed to see what was happening. Later, they saw a constable rushing over, saying that someone had been shot and killed by a thug.

▲ A Young Man Lying in a Pool of Blood A Chinese constable on patrol in the area arrived after hearing the news and saw a young man around 26 or 27 years old lying in a pool of blood. Upon closer inspection of his clothing, he looked like a businessman, wearing a blue serge jacket, black silk pants, Chinese leather shoes, and white cotton socks. He was round-faced and plump. The injuries were to the head, with one gunshot wound to the temple, and one gunshot wound to the back. Both bullets did not exit.

▲ Testimony from Eyewitnesses After the incident, eyewitnesses said that the deceased was walking in the alley with a young woman when a man in short clothes suddenly came up from behind, looking angry. When he approached the young man, he pulled out a gun and shot the deceased in the head and then in the back, resulting in the fatal attack. The thug then escaped through nearby Xingmaoli.

▲ Results of Investigation by Chinese and Foreign Detectives The area is under the jurisdiction of the Xinzha Police Station. Chinese and foreign detectives drove to the scene to investigate and searched the alleys thoroughly, but found nothing. They sent the deceased to the Ferren Road autopsy center and scheduled an autopsy for today. The deceased died instantly, and his name is unknown.

Westerners Penetrate Remote Regions

▲ Recounting the Experience Upon Return to Shanghai

The Shanghai Times reported that in September of last year, Milligan, an Englishman from the Old MacKenzie & Co., and Gordon, an Englishman from the Asiatic Petroleum Company, returned to their home countries from Shanghai. They suddenly had the urge to explore and took a route through the southwest frontier to Burma, where they boarded a ship. They luckily avoided diseases and bandits along the way and arrived in Burma safely after three months and two weeks. They took a boat back to Europe. Rohl, a German merchant from Chongqing, also joined them along the way. Milligan recently returned to Shanghai last week, and Rohl will also return to China around May or June. However, Gordon may not return. According to Milligan, they departed from Shanghai on September 8 last year and took a boat to Chongqing. He learned that Rohl had already left and hurried to catch up. When they arrived in Yazhou, they rented donkeys and horses and traveled along the main road to Ningyuan. However, they had to dismount and walk due to the mountain dangers. The places they passed through were relatively peaceful, with only a scarcity of products. Below Ningyuan, they originally planned to travel southwest to Lijiang, but due to a local army rebellion against its commander, the road was blocked. They had no choice but to continue along the main road south to Huili. There were no bandit incidents along the way. It is also possible to reach Lijiang from the west of Huili, but due to bandits in Yongbei, they continued along the main road used by merchants to the south to Longkai on the Jinsha River. From there, they crossed the river and entered Yunnan Province. At that time, countless merchants were waiting to cross the river at Longkai. They joined the group, but the guards initially suspected them of being defeated soldiers returning from Sichuan and refused them entry. After they explained, they were allowed to cross the river, which delayed them for two days. After entering Yunnan Province, they took a shortcut west from Makai (transliteration) to Chuxiong, where they rejoined the main road and continued west through Dali, Yongchang, and Tengyue to Bhamo in Burma. From Yazhou to Bhamo, the mountains were steep and difficult to travel. Below Bhamo, the terrain gradually flattened. They took a boat along the Irrawaddy River to Katha, then took a train through Mandalay and arrived in Rangoon on December 22. The journey from Shanghai to Rangoon was over 3,500 miles. Although they experienced hardships along the way, they found it interesting and were treated well by the people and officials everywhere they went. Food was mostly purchased locally, and it was cheap and delicious. They hired a Chinese cook in Chongqing to accompany them and act as a translator along the way. The largest wild animal they encountered in Yunnan Province was the wolf. Because they were eager to travel, they did not have time to go hunting in the deep mountains. Although they did not encounter bandits along the way, they often saw traces of banditry. Villages and towns in remote areas were mostly in ruins.

The Tugboat Chartered by Shenhu Was Robbed and Kidnapped

▲ Six People Kidnapped ▲ The Bandit Leader Addicted to Opium

The Shenhu class of small steamships of the Merchants' Inland Navigation Steamship Bureau has a total of three ships: Hengji, Hengde, and Hengsheng. Each small steamship tows three ships belonging to the company: one exclusively for transporting passengers and goods from Linghu, and two for Nanxun and Huzhou. Each time they arrive at a destination, they detach the company ships, and the small steamship continues forward. However, Linghu is located inland and cannot be reached directly. It can only be towed to Pingwang, where another small steamship, Dehe (also owned by the Merchants' Bureau), tows it into Linghu. The other day (the 13th), a chartered ship (i.e., a company ship) owned by Yang Wenrong of Wuxi, carrying more than 20 passengers and goods, was towed by Dehe from Linghu. At 3:00 PM, when it arrived at the place of Sitintze, north of Niaozhen North Gate (commonly known as Youtian Wuri Tou), which is the border area of Wujiang, Tongxiang, and Wuxing counties in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces (commonly known as the "three-no-management area"), a place where salt smugglers and bandits often appear, a large bandit ship and thirteen small boats suddenly appeared. The bandit gang consisted of one hundred and twenty to thirty people, all fully loaded with Lake bandits, who ordered the small steamship to stop. The bandits jumped onto the small steamship and the company ship, each holding quick-firing guns and bayonets, and began searching separately. All of the more than 20 passengers were not spared. Silver dollars, clothes, bedding, goods, and the valuables in the accounting room were all robbed onto the bandit ship. Before leaving, six people (four men and two women) were taken hostage, including Yang Liuquan, the son of the owner of the chartered ship (i.e., the company ship), and his two daughters-in-law. The rest were all passengers. The bandits searched the ship for an hour, taking all the valuables. The ship that the bandit leader was on seemed to be the bandit leader's ship. There were three female bandits, dressed in luxurious clothes. The bandit leader was addicted to opium, and a couch was laid out in the cabin, where he was inhaling the fumes. Some bandits were also cooking opium in the aft cabin. With a command from the bandit leader, the bandits returned to their small boats, each small boat seemingly led by a small leader. All the stolen valuables and cash were moved onto the bandit leader's large ship, and then they each weighed anchor and sailed away quickly. The shipowner has now reported the incident to the Merchants' Bureau, which has reported it to the Wujiang, Tongxiang, and Wuxing County Public Security Bureaus, both land and water, to send police to jointly investigate the stolen goods and bandits and bring them to justice.

Seized Fake Official Seal in Bandit Lair

The Seal Represents the Party for National Salvation

Jiangsu Tonghai Garrison Commander

▲Anti-revolutionary Connections in the Kidnapping Case

▲All Transferred to the Higher Court for Interrogation

Xiao Da, the son of Wang Bin-yan, a prominent businessman, was kidnapped on his way home from school in Zhabei a few days ago, as reported in the newspapers. The military and police authorities of both the Chinese and foreign concessions have been paying close attention to this case. The Hongkou police received a tip-off the other day that some kidnappers would be passing along Broadway Road at 2:00 PM. Detective Wei Jinfu, along with Detective He Ruhai, Officer He Xiaozhi, and Western Detective Si Wen, were dispatched to Broadway Road to lie in wait. At 2:00 PM, they apprehended Lin Jin-han, a native of Tongzhou, and took him back to the police station. According to his confession, his accomplices were hiding at No. 1132 Tongchun Lane, Gongping Road. The detectives proceeded to that location and apprehended Zhang Bing-sheng (also known as Zhang Mei-tong), his mistress Zhang Wang-shi. They also found a fake official seal inside the house, which read "Jiangsu Tonghai Garrison Commander of the Party for National Salvation," as well as a fake letter of appointment commissioning Zhang Bing-sheng as the garrison commander, and other reactionary documents. In addition, they found two fake car permit license plates. According to Zhang's confession at the police station, firearms were hidden inside the house at No. 97 Chongqing Road. Detective Zhu then went to that location to search and confiscated two thousand yuan in banknotes from the Northeast Provinces, but did not find any firearms. Zhao Jia-ying, who lived in the house, was also taken to the police station and detained for strict interrogation. Given the presence of anti-revolutionary evidence mixed in with the case, the defendants and all the evidence were transferred to the Higher Court yesterday morning, where Judge Du Fu-yao specially opened the second courtroom to hear the case. Mr. Ru Bao-yi, the police lawyer, briefly described the case, presented the various pieces of evidence and banknotes, and then Chinese and Western detectives reported on the circumstances of the arrest of the defendants. Judge Du first interrogated the defendant Lin Jin-han, who claimed that he had been farming in his hometown and had only recently come to Shanghai. He denied any knowledge of the kidnapping. Zhang Bing-sheng also claimed that he had been farming in his hometown and that after coming to Shanghai, he lived on Gongping Road. He said that the fake car permits were brought to him by a friend in a package and stored with him. He claimed that he initially did not know what was inside the package. However, a man named Lian Ying had discussed with him the possibility of committing a kidnapping, but he had refused because he considered it illegal. As for the various documents, he said that a Mr. Liu, currently in Tokyo, Japan, had introduced him to the leader, who issued the documents to him and others. Zhang Wang-shi claimed that she had been living with Zhang Bing-sheng since November of last year, for only a short time, and that she did not know what he was doing. Zhao Jia-ying claimed that he had indeed been issued a handgun when he was working as a copier in the detective squad, but he no longer had it, and there were no firearms or ammunition in his home. The banknotes from the Northeast Provinces were brought by a friend as collateral for a loan of twenty yuan. Judge Du, after hearing the testimonies, ordered that the case be re-investigated. The defendants were then returned to the police station for detention. It is still uncertain whether the kidnapping case is related to the abduction of Mr. Wang's son.

City Public Security Bureau Receives Fake Letter of Appointment

▲Smudged Rubbings on the Letter

▲Possible Frame-up Involved

The City Public Security Bureau recently received a letter from someone named Yang Yu-long, alleging that his brother, Yu-liang, who lives in Yihe Village, Pudong, had been appointed as a commander by the counter-revolutionary "fake commander" Xu Chong-zhi and was carrying out sabotage. The letter included a letter of appointment, in which the three characters for Yang Yu-liang appeared to have been added on top of another character after it had been erased with rubber. The year, originally 1929, had been forcibly changed from "eight" to "nine," and the month, December, was also smudged with rubber, clearly indicating that the fake letter of appointment had been intentionally altered. The Bureau, suspecting other motives, ordered the police in the third district of Pudong to summon Yang Yu-liang to the district for questioning. He claimed to be fifty-two years old, a native of Shandong, making a living by running a small teahouse in Yihe Village. He said that he had a wife and seven or eight children. He owned a small boat, which he used to row to various warships to beg for steamed buns and miscellaneous items. He said that his family was very poor, that he did not have a brother, and that there was no such person as Yang Yu-long. He claimed that it was a malicious accusation by his enemies. After verifying the testimony, the district chief sent the case to the General Bureau for disposal.

Hua Cui-ying Petitions for Recognition as Daughter

▲Father Runs Soap Factory, Daughter Works to Support Mother

▲Driven Away for Nine Years, Treated as a Stranger

▲Failed to Reach Agreement in Court with 500 Yuan Offer

▲Lawyers Go Outside to Mediate

Hua Guan-chen, a Ningbo native and owner of the Henry Soap Factory at Wangjiazuijiao in the South City, is being sued by Hua Cui-ying, the daughter of his concubine Hua Li-shi, who retained attorney Gu Ji-rong to file a petition in the District Court for recognition as his daughter. The petition states that the plaintiff is the biological daughter of the defendant, Hua Guan-chen. The plaintiff's mother, Hua Li-shi, married the defendant as a concubine in the 31st year of the Guangxu reign (Qing dynasty) and gave birth to a daughter (the plaintiff). However, since 1921, the defendant and the plaintiff’s mother, Hua Li-shi, had repeatedly been involved in litigation. After reaching a settlement, the defendant insisted on driving away the plaintiff’s biological mother, Hua Li-shi, and disowned the plaintiff as his daughter. At that time, the plaintiff was thirteen years old, alone and unable to support herself, and had to live with her mother, barely surviving. Nine years have passed. Now, the mother and daughter rely on their labor to make a living, struggling to eat and dress properly. The father treats his concubine as a stranger, and the father and daughter are like enemies. The future is bleak, and it is likely that they will end up in a ditch. The defendant owns a large fortune and is extremely extravagant, yet he abandons his own daughter. His intentions are clear. Therefore, the plaintiff requests a judgment ordering him to recognize her. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Zhao Zhen-hai specially opened the second courtroom to hear the case. The defendant did not appear, but retained attorney Yao Yong-li to represent him in court. Hua Cui-ying, the plaintiff, testified that she was twenty-two years old, a native of Ningbo, living at No. 37 Tongxing Street, Yangjiazhai, Pudong. She is currently working as a tin foil packer at the British American Tobacco Company. Hua Li-shi testified that she was forty-one years old, living with her daughter, relying entirely on her daughter's hard work to make a living. She is responsible for cooking and washing clothes at home. The judge asked the plaintiff, "What is your request?" Hua Cui-ying replied, "I request the defendant to recognize me as his daughter and to inherit his property." The judge said, "Is it better to reach a settlement in this case?" (Answer) "I do not want to settle."

"In January of this year, I returned to the defendant's home and was pushed out by my father and others." (Question) "Are you born to Li-shi?" (Answer) "Yes." (Question) "Before your mother left the defendant, did you live together or separately?" (Answer) "Together, because the first wife, named A-xiang, was extremely fierce and often mistreated my mother." (Question) "How many children did your mother give birth to?" (Answer) "Only me. The first wife gave birth to two sons and three daughters." (Question) "How much property do you want?" (Answer) "Please allocate according to the court." The judge said, "Property is another issue. Your current petition is for recognition as a daughter. Only after that is determined will we talk about property issues. But how much property does your father have?" (Answer) "The Henry Soap Factory at Wangjiazuijiao and properties in Zhenhai, my hometown, are worth about 100,000 yuan." In the past, my father gave me away to be a daughter-in-law, but I refused, so I live with my mother. Now I can earn six or seven dimes a day." At this point, she took out a copper tag from the British American Tobacco Company and presented it to the court. The judge read it and returned it to her. (Question) "Have you been betrothed?" (Answer) "No." The judge said, "Then how about your father be responsible for the expenses of your betrothal and all the dowry for your wedding in the future?" (Answer) "My father is only willing to give four or five hundred yuan, which is not enough, because when my father's eldest daughter got married, the dowry cost about five thousand yuan." At this point, the judge ordered the defendant's lawyer to state the defendant's age, place of origin, address, and occupation. Lawyer Yao stated that the defendant, Hua Guan-chen, was fifty-seven years old, a native of Zhenhai, Ningbo, residing at No. 15 Xiao Jiuhua, outside the Dadongmen, and running the Henry Soap Factory at Wangjiazuijiao. The judge asked if the plaintiff was the defendant's daughter. Lawyer Yao replied, "Yes, born to Li-shi." The judge tried to mediate a settlement in court. The defendant was only willing to pay 500 yuan, which the plaintiff did not agree to. The judge then ordered the lawyers of both parties to mediate outside the court for one week. If no settlement could be reached, another hearing would be held. The court was then adjourned.

Robbers Cruelly Burn Victim's Lower Body

Xu Jia-tao, a resident of Xujiazhai in Wusong West, is about forty years old and has a modest income, making him a target for robbers. At around 11:00 PM the other night, more than ten robbers, armed with sharp blades, broke down the door and rushed into the bedroom. Xu's family members, who were already asleep, were awakened from their dreams and were bound by the robbers, who pointed sharp blades at them, forbidding them to make any noise. The robbers then freely searched for money, clothing, and other items, looting everything. The robbers were not satisfied and forced the victim to reveal the location of his hidden silver. Xu claimed that he had no money. The robbers, becoming enraged, suddenly had a bizarre idea: they stripped the male and female victims of their pants and burned their lower bodies with torches. Xu and his wife screamed in agony. The robbers stabbed Xu's legs several times and then fled with their loot, shouting and yelling. It is said that Xu's injuries were minor, but his wife, Li-shi, suffered severe burns to her lower body.

Two Passengers Missing from British Ship from Hong Kong

▲Telegram Sent to Hong Kong to Investigate

According to the Da Wan Bao, two passengers went missing on the British ship Kashgar on its way from Hong Kong to Shanghai. Their whereabouts are still unknown. The two men are named He Bo-lian (transliteration) and Liu Ze (transliteration). Both boarded the ship in Hong Kong but disappeared en route. The ship’s officers were immediately notified, and a thorough search of the entire ship was conducted for several hours. The two men's belongings were found, consisting only of a handbag. No letters were left behind. Inquiries were made to all the passengers, but no clues were found. Their luggage consisted only of a handbag and a basket of fruit, with nothing else. Based on this observation, it seems that they boarded the ship specifically to commit suicide by jumping into the sea. After the ship arrived in Shanghai today (the 14th), another thorough search of the entire ship was conducted, but no other clues were found. The company has now telegraphed Hong Kong, requesting that they investigate the background of the two men.

City Public Utilities Bureau Guides Electric Company in Reorganizing High-Voltage Underground Cables

In recent years, the China General Edison Company has been increasing its electricity supply, and the load has been increasing daily. The existing circuits in various locations are insufficient. In order to meet the needs, the company recently built a new substation No. 1 at the intersection of Guohuo Road and Puyu New Road, which has been completed. It is now planning to add and replace high-voltage underground cables on various routes, mainly: (1) Adding electrical cables between the power plant, substation No. 11, and the new and old substations No. 1. (2) Burying a cable from the factory to the proposed substation No. 24 on Jumen Road. (3) Replacing the cable to the Jiangnan Shipyard and adding another cable as a backup line for the domestic water company. (4) Adding equipment lines to the arsenal substation. (5) Connecting the proposed substation No. 25 behind the manufacturing bureau to substations No. 1 and No. 14. (6) Replacing the original cables between substations No. 2 and No. 11 and between substations No. 11 and No. 7 and removing the underground cables from the power plant to the old No. 1 substation and from the old No. 1 substation to No. 2 substation. The City Public Utilities Bureau reviewed the plan and deemed it generally appropriate, but noted that there were points to be supplemented, such as the submission of diagrams for the new substations that have been built or are to be built for verification, and that common and standby cables should not be buried in the same location. If they cannot be separated, the burial method should be improved. The bureau also suggested extending the standby line to the arsenal to substation No. 24 to serve as a backup line for that substation as well. The bureau has issued its comments and ordered the company to comply accordingly.

Achievements of Qianyi Traumatology Hospital

The Qianyi Traumatology Hospital in Zhabei was founded by philanthropists Chen Bing-qian and Wang Bin-yan, specializing in the treatment of traumatic injuries and internal and external rheumatism. It provides completely free treatment and does not charge fees. Its director, Mr. Zhang De-yi, treats patients, regardless of their wealth, with the utmost sincerity. His skills are miraculous. Western doctors find it difficult to deal with broken backs and fractured legs, or even require amputation, but once treated by the famous doctor Zhang, life and limbs can be preserved without pain. His wife, Ms. Zheng Ying, is also skilled in medicine and assists Mr. Zhang in this charitable cause. Her contribution is not small. Therefore, the hospital's operations have been developing in recent years, and the threshold for seeking treatment is being crossed. There is no fixed fund for its operating expenses; it relies entirely on fundraising. The local philanthropist Mr. Du Yue-sheng donates a huge sum of 300 yuan per month. There are also many other sporadic donations. If it is still not enough, Chen, Wang, and Zhang will contribute from their own pockets. This kind of charitable organization is second to none in Shanghai, so people in society praise it. On the occasion of the fifth anniversary, a report on the achievements was submitted. After reviewing the photos of major injuries that have been treated, it is clear that there is a magical technique to bring the dead back to life and preserve the body. The above are the small photos of Mr. and Mrs. Zhang.

Problem of Relaxation of Rickshaw Licenses in the Concessions

▲Zheng Li-min Represents the Petition

▲Chen Jia-chang Goes to Negotiate

Rickshaw dealer Zheng Li-min previously complained that the rickshaw merchant association of the Public Concession monopolized rickshaw licenses, resulting in uneven distribution among rickshaw dealers. He also noted that the number of rickshaw pullers was increasing daily, resulting in a shortage of vehicles and frequent quarrels and fights over pulling rickshaws. He had taken film footage of the brawls and had repeatedly submitted petitions to the Shanghai Special City Government, requesting that the British Concession Authorities be consulted to relax the issuance of rickshaw licenses in order to meet the demand and maintain the livelihoods of the poor. The City Government sent personnel to consult with the Concession Authorities, but the Concession Authorities stated that the board of directors had already decided on the issue of relaxing the licenses. Under the current circumstances, there was no need to relax the licenses, and there was even the possibility of reducing the number of licenses in the future. The City Government clearly issued an order on the matter. Now, Zheng Li-min has submitted the film of the brawls over rickshaws, along with a detailed account of the number of rickshaw pullers unemployed in Shanghai, to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that it grant relief and promptly consult with the British Concession Authorities to cancel the quota of 5,161 rickshaw licenses stipulated in 1924 and issue a sufficient number to save the lives of the common people. Minister Wang read the petition and understood the situation. Yesterday, he instructed Director Chen of the Shanghai Office to consult with the British Concession Authorities to increase the number of rickshaw licenses in order to maintain the livelihood of the common people.

Man Speaking Nonsense with Reactionary Leaflets in his Possession

▲Claims to Have Picked them up from the Ground

Yesterday morning, a young man, wearing short clothes, was walking along Lan-ni Ferry in Pudong when he suddenly suffered a nervous breakdown and was talking to himself, displaying both joy and anger. Lang Xun-ling, a policeman from the Third District of the Public Security Bureau, saw him and went forward to question him. The man was talking nonsense. Several dozens of reactionary leaflets, two dollars in large bills, four dimes in small bills, and a copper tag were found on his person. He was taken to the district office. He claimed to be Yu Wen-sheng, twenty-six years old, from Tongzhou, and lived in a thatched hut at the Fenshan Wharf in Pudong, working as a rickshaw puller. When asked where the leaflets came from, he said he picked them up from the ground. The district chief verified the testimony and ordered that his family members be summoned to investigate the truth of the matter.

Interrogation of Bandits Repeatedly Involved in Kidnapping Cases

Yan Ru-ling, a Ningbo native and comprador of the former French-owned Oriental Fur Company, residing at No. 1325 Lafayette Road in the French Concession, was kidnapped from his new home on the 23rd of last month and held in a bandit den at No. 356 Jin Shen-fu Road. The case was investigated by the special agency detectives and supervisors of the French police, Jin Jiu-lin, detectives Li Yao-long, Mao Jin-gen, Qian Yu-min, and patrolmen Zhou Yao-ting, Zhou Bing-cheng, Zhang Zi-ying, Zhou Bu-guang, and Qin You-yu, who went to the bandit den, captured the kidnappers Zhang Hong-xiang, Lu Pei-zhou, Wang A-song, Fang You-shan, Tao Jin-bao, Luo Shi-sheng, Chen Lian-gen, Wang A-da, and the person involved, Zhao Ren-mao, a total of nine people. They also confiscated three handguns, one Mauser pistol, and more than twenty bullets, rescued the victim, and took them to the police station. The victim was escorted home. The matter has been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday, they were sent to the French court for investigation. Judge Zhu Qi, together with French Consul Du He, presided over the criminal court for interrogation. Detective Supervisor Jin Jiu-lin was the first to go to court to report the situation, saying that the defendants had successively kidnapped Lu Cheng-yao, a wealthy businessman on Lafayette Road, and Qian Chang-gan, from No. 5 Xixianfang, West Ames Road, and divided the ransom money. He also said that the first defendant, Zhang Hong-xiang, had committed theft six or seven years ago, was detained, and sentenced to five years. He had not been released for long before committing another serious crime. When they went to arrest them, they opened fire to resist arrest. He asked for strict investigation and presented the handguns and Mauser pistol. Next, Attorney Ba He, representing the plaintiff Yan Ru-ling, described the kidnapping and interrogated Zhang Hong-xiang, who stated that he was forty-three years old, a native of Tongzhou, and had committed a crime before and been dealt with by the court. This time, Lu Pei-zhou invited him to Anle Palace on March 10 to discuss kidnapping the plaintiff, Yan Ru-ling, because Yan was the father-in-law of Lu Pei-zhou's brother, Lu Cheng-yao, so he knew that Yan had considerable wealth. First, Lu accompanied Wu to Lafayette Road to identify Yan Ru-ling's appearance. Then, a civilian borrowed a car with the number 1920 from Chen Lian-gen and changed the number to 2921. He then invited the fugitive Dai Qing-yun and Fang You-shan, Tao Jin-bao, and Luo Shi-sheng to go there on the 22nd, disguised as painters, and waited inside for a long time. When they did not see the plaintiff arrive, they returned to the inn. The next day, they went again, still disguised as painters and working inside. Soon, the plaintiff arrived. He and Dai Qing-yun each took out handguns, first threatening the bodyguard and seizing his handgun. Then, they dragged the plaintiff onto their car and sent him to No. 356 Jin Shen-fu Road to hide. He did not know how the detectives were arrested by a civilian at No. 769 Taolin Lane, Chengdu Road. The civilian accompanied the patrolman to Jin Shen-fu Road to rescue the victim. He did not know how they opened fire to resist arrest. He also said that he was not present at the kidnapping of Qian Chang-gan, although he had also received 300 yuan in the division of the spoils. This time, he knew the law and broke the law, and his crime was unforgivable. If the court sentenced him to death, he had a wife and young children who relied on him. However, his cousin Zhang Fu-qing owed him 400 yuan and eight small cars. He asked to summon his cousin to court to recover the money and hand over the cars to his wife for living expenses. The Chinese and Western officials approved it. Lu Pei-zhou stated that he was a native of Tongzhou. The previous year, Zhang A-si, who was still at large, proposed and discussed the matter with him to kidnap his brother Lu Cheng-yao. Afterwards, he received 2,000 yuan in the division of the spoils. Then he continued to kidnap Qian Chang-gan and received 800 yuan. On March 10 of the same year, he proposed and invited Zhang Hong-xiang to kidnap his relative Yan Ru-ling, but he was not present at the time. Wang A-gen stated that he had been working as a partner in a certain company. A few days ago, a friend Xu A-bao invited him to go out to see a play. After the play, Xu tricked him to a place on Bedan Road, where several accomplices ganged up on him, beat him, and shot him in the right arm. Afterwards, he went to Tongde Hospital for treatment. The French patrolman found out that he was an accomplice in the kidnapping of the plaintiff, which was a complete injustice. At this point, Supervisor Jin said that he saw the defendant Wang A-gen opening fire to resist arrest that day. They also opened fire to fight back, wounding his arm. Wang fled with his injury and sought treatment at the hospital. He was found and arrested. Zhang Hong-xiang testified that it was Wang A-gen who drove the car when kidnapping the plaintiff. Chen Lian-gen stated that he was working as a driver for the Li family. On March 23, his friend Zhang Hong-xiang came to borrow the car, saying he was loading opium. He did not know about the kidnapping. The rest of his statement was evasive. Fang You-shan, Tao Jin-bao, Luo Shi-sheng, and Wang A-da all stated that they had been invited by Zhang Hong-xiang to go to the plaintiff's new home and pretend to be painters. Later, they were in the bandit den guarding the victim. Zhao Ren-mao stated that he was driving a car and knew nothing about the case. He asked for leniency. After consultation, the Chinese and Western officials ordered that the defendants be detained and await further interrogation at a later date.

Extortion Case Appeal

Zhou Fugen and Wang Ziqing, formerly near Broadway Road in Yangshupu, were arrested for extorting money from Xu Yongqing. They were handed over to the former Provisional Court for trial. Zhou was sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment, and Wang to one year and eight months. Dissatisfied, the two convicts hired Lawyer Fan Gang to appeal. Yesterday afternoon, Song Yuan, the Presiding Judge of the High Court's Criminal Division, along with Judges Ye Zaigi and Gao Junxiang, opened the court for a retrial. Chief Prosecutor Wang also attended to perform his duties. After clarifying the facts in court, arguments began. First, Lawyer Fan spoke on behalf of the two appellants, Zhou and Wang. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, also wanted to respond, but the Presiding Judge stated that the case did not require the police to present their case, as it was not related to the police. The lawyer argued that the case was initially prosecuted by the police, so he still requested permission to express his opinion. If an oral statement was not allowed, he would submit a written statement. The court then granted the lawyer permission to respond. Later, Zhou and Wang were ordered to be returned to custody, and the date for sentencing was set.

Rickshaw Puller Commits Suicide Due to Economic Hardship

Qian Haihai, a rickshaw puller, lived at No. 2 Dongxing Lane, Disiwei Road, Zhabei. He was 38 years old and from Danyang. Due to the oppression of his living environment and extreme poverty, he became weary of life. The day before yesterday afternoon, he committed suicide by consuming opium. Ai Hanming Dies by Poisoning

▲Distressed that His Wife Did Not Return, He Resorted to This

Ai Hanming, 22 years old, from Jiading, worked at the Hongkou Cigarette Factory. His wife, Zhou, also 22, from Huangdu, had been married for over three years but had not yet had children. The couple's relationship was known to be very close. Ai found it difficult to make a living in his hometown, so in September of last year, he brought his wife to Shanghai and rented a loft room in the flat-roofed house of the second landlord, Su Weisheng, at the intersection of Singapore Road in West Shanghai. They lived together. After Ai started working at the cigarette factory, he would return home every two or three days for the night, which became his habit. Zhou also went to work at a nearby sock factory but soon stopped. However, Ai's monthly wages were very meager, and he often worried about not being able to make ends meet. As a result, the couple inevitably had some quarrels. At the beginning of last month, during an argument, Ai, filled with resentment, bought opium paste in an attempt to commit suicide. Fortunately, he was discovered early and saved by a doctor. Later, Zhou, seeing the high cost of living and the meager wages of her husband, and hoping to reduce the burden, agreed with her husband in the middle of last month to go out and work as a servant for a few months, then find another way. Thus, Zhou went to work as a servant for the Chen family at No. 70 Cunchan Lane, Wujiaochang, near their home. Ai would return home every few days to reunite with his wife. The day before yesterday (the 13th) at 6:00 PM, Ai returned home from the factory and went to bed in the loft. After a while, he called out to the second landlord, Su, and asked him to go to the Chen family in Cunchan Lane and ask his wife, Zhou, to return home immediately because he suddenly felt unwell and it could not be delayed. Su went immediately to tell her, but Zhou refused to return home, saying, "What is wrong with him? Let him die if he wants to!" Su then relayed this response. Soon after, Su, living below the loft, only heard Ai sighing and breathing, assuming it was because he was upset that his wife would not return. When the clock struck nine, the second landlord, Su, suddenly felt that Ai was quiet and silent. He took a lamp up to the loft and saw Ai lying motionless. He called out to him, but there was no response. His face was already purple, and his breath was faint. Greatly alarmed, he knew that Ai had taken poison. Su immediately called his wife to return home and then reported to the Sixth District Police Station. Upon receiving the report, Section Chief Duan immediately sent police to take the poisoned man, Zhou, the second landlord Su Weisheng, and the lodger Jin Xinggui back to the district. The poisoned man was immediately sent to the Red Cross Hospital on Haige Road for treatment. After examination by the doctor, it was confirmed that he had consumed opium paste. However, because the dose was too large and the time was too late, he was in a near-death state and could not be saved. He died at 0:30 AM yesterday. Yesterday morning, Section Chief Duan conducted separate interrogations. The second landlord, Su Weisheng, testified that he was 27 years old and from Changzhou. The lodger, Jin Xinggui, testified that he was 35 years old and from Linhai. Ai Zhou, the wife of the deceased, testified that she was 22 years old and from Huangdu. She also presented a note written by her husband, Ai Hanming, before the incident (the note read: "Owes A Chang 6 yuan at No. 1022, Lane 2, Huade Lane, Hed Road, must be repaid in full without delay"). After receiving the testimonies, Section Chief Duan ordered that Zhou be temporarily detained and instructed the local guarantor, Tan Hefu, to report to the District Court and request that someone be sent to examine the body for further investigation.

The Japanese Navy's First Overseas Stationed China Fleet warship Toba, which has been stationed in Shanghai for a long time, received orders from Commander Minai yesterday to sail to the Yangtze River for defense. It is scheduled to leave Shanghai today (the 15th) and enter the Yangtze River. After passing through Zhenjiang, Nanjing, Wuhu, Jiujiang, and Daye, it will arrive in Hankou, expected on the 28th.

Yesterday morning at 10:30, Prosecutor Guo Wei, accompanied by a clerk and forensic doctors, went to examine the body. Next, the deceased's wife, Zhu Guan, testified, "My husband has always had dizziness, which often occurs. This time, it must be a recurrence of dizziness. There is no other reason. Chen Yuemei and Wu Dekang Fight Over Child

▲The Legal Wife Suddenly Arrives

▲Scissors Are Drawn

Chen Yuemei, a 24-year-old woman from Ningbo, lost her parents early and had no property or relatives to rely on. Her situation was dire. After a long time, her livelihood became increasingly difficult. She met Wu Dekang, a Wuxi native who worked at the Rongxing Machinery Factory. Wu, noticing that the woman was beautiful, gradually seduced her, falsely claiming that he was not yet married. The woman also needed support, so she complied, and they fell in love and lived together at No. 19 Meiji Lane, Triangle Street, Nanshi. When the woman realized that Wu already had a legal wife living in his hometown, she silently acknowledged that the die was cast and could only wait and see what happened. More than four years had passed, and she had given birth to a son who was already three years old, and was still six months pregnant. Unexpectedly, in the middle of last month, Wu's wife suddenly came to Shanghai from her hometown, pretending to be visiting. Wu feared that the woman might change her mind because of this, so he gave his three-year-old son to his wife to take home. The woman was furious upon learning the truth, and the two sides often argued, demanding the return of the child, but to no avail. At approximately 7:00 PM the day before yesterday, another conflict broke out over the child. Wu was also enraged and grabbed a pair of scissors from the table, intending to stab her. Fortunately, Fang Zaihao, a Ningbo native living with them, saw it and rushed to stop him. Fearing a major disaster, he went outside and called Wang Ganchen, the security guard of the 25th Post, to come. They took the man and woman back to the First Precinct of the First District. During the preliminary hearing by the chief, the woman requested a divorce. He ordered that a document be prepared and sent to the Shanghai District Court for review.

Incoming Correspondence

Labor Statistics Work and Plans (Continued)

▲Shanghai Special City Social Bureau

(D) Survey of Workers' Living Standards: The survey of workers' lives has at least two main purposes. The first is to understand the living environment of workers and the minimum living expenses of a worker's family. The second is to obtain the goods and quantities that should be included in the cost of living index. According to economic principles, work efficiency and living environment are closely related. For example, workers who have a comfortable life, proper physical and mental development, and education are generally more efficient and capable than workers who have poor living environments and no education. Their productivity is naturally also greater. Therefore, if workers can have a comfortable living environment and receive considerable education, the overall national economy can increase a great deal of production. This is the biggest reason we want to study the living conditions of workers. Recently, the National Government promulgated the Factory Law, which stipulates that the minimum wage for workers should be based on the living conditions of local workers. Therefore, a survey of living standards is even more urgent. However, what are the current living conditions of workers? Are they able to enjoy the benefits of modern material civilization equally? What is the minimum living cost for an average worker's family? These questions cannot be clarified without a cost of living survey. In this survey, we need to know at least the following items: the distribution of workers' families by population, age, gender, and occupation; the sources and amount of income; the average household expenditure on food, clothing, housing, lighting and fuel, and other expenses; the average number of people living in each room; and the minimum living cost. (E) Cost of Living Index and Real Wage Index: The survey of living standards and the cost of living index are different. The former is a static survey that investigates the living conditions of workers in a certain period. The latter is a dynamic survey that investigates the historical trends of changes in living expenses. We all know that the prices of consumer goods often fluctuate due to market supply and demand. When prices rise, the cost of living is high. When prices fall, the cost of living is low. Therefore, the cost of living changes with the rise and fall of prices. The cost of living index is based on the results of the survey of living standards. According to the consumption of various items, the weight of each item in the index is determined. Then, its price is investigated to find the cost of maintaining the original living standard compared with the base year. Thus, an index is compiled. Therefore, with the cost of living index, we can know whether this year's cost of living is higher or lower than the base year by a certain percentage. It is most fair to solve the wage problem based on this. It is best to compile a separate classification index for food expenses, housing expenses, clothing expenses, lighting and fuel expenses, and miscellaneous expenses to observe the individual changes in each category of consumption. The total index is formed by combining the various classification indexes, which represents the changes in the general cost of living. The cost of living index has a purpose, which is to measure the strength of the purchasing power of money to find the real wage index. When prices rise, the value of money falls or the purchasing power is weak. When prices fall, the value of money rises or the purchasing power is strong. The wages that workers earn are used to buy supplies to maintain their lives. However, since the purchasing power of money often changes, the real value of wages also increases or decreases accordingly. For example, if it used to be possible to maintain a living with a wage of 30 yuan, if prices rise by 20 percent, then 36 yuan is now required because the value of 36 yuan is equivalent to the previous 30 yuan. In other words, items that used to cost 30 yuan now cost 36 yuan to buy. Therefore, if we want to ensure that the actual value of wages does not change, then in addition to compiling a money wage index, we must also consider the increase or decrease in the purchasing power of money. Since the cost of living index is a thermometer for measuring the purchasing power of money, dividing the cost of living index by the money wage index and then multiplying by 100 yields the real wage index. The meaning is the index that measures the change in the real value of wages. Since the real wage index can indicate whether the wages that workers receive are sufficient to maintain their original living standards, we can easily plan remedial methods. (F) Industrial Accidents: Under the machine production system, unexpected accidents during work are almost inevitable for workers. This directly harms the workers themselves. On the factory side, losses are also significant, such as machine damage, injury compensation, replacement of novices, and reduced production efficiency. All of these things are also indirectly a loss to society. Recently, industrial accidents in various countries have received great attention, and efforts are being made to improve disaster prevention and preparation. However, to understand the root causes and prevent them, statistics must be relied upon. Important items include the number of accidents and people in each industry, the causes of accidents, the nature of the accidents, the injured parts, the degree, the number of days, the number of work hours and wages lost due to injury, and the cost of pensions. (To be continued)
