Free Talk

Random Thoughts on Spring Outings

— Yang Jia Yi

▲There is a true and false distinction in spring outings. Artists' spring outings are the truest, while lovers' spring outings are the falsest.

▲If you like to take a cursory look, then you should not go on a spring outing. Because if you do, the truly beautiful scenery of nature will be far away from you.

▲When going on a spring outing, you must not be lazy. Because if you are lazy, your legs will not be willing to stroll leisurely.

▲A person's interest in spring outings is highest in youth. Because at this time, the weak hearts of men and women are sprouting like plants.

▲In the eyes of city dwellers, a spring outing is a treasure. In the eyes of villagers, a spring outing is a toy.

▲The union of men and women is easiest during a spring outing. Because at this time, they have all been baptized by nature, making it easiest for them to attract each other.

▲Shorthand and spring outings are closely related. If you can record everything during a spring outing, then the spring outing can have something to rely on.

▲The happiness of a poor person's life is unattainable, except for spring outings.

▲Spring outings not only allow you to fully enjoy the spring scenery, but also scare away your demons of worry.

▲When you go on a spring outing with your lover, you must not talk about the beauty or ugliness of nature. Because if you do, your sensitive partner is likely to become jealous.

▲Dr. McDougall of the United States said, "A person who can be idle in the bright spring sun will be able to enjoy his true happiness." Ah, what a profound truth! (See American Magazine)

A Record of Distinguished Guests Enjoying Scenic Spots

— Bai Xi

Spring's chill is accompanied by frequent rains. I am beset by both laziness and illness. The floral season is nearing its end, yet I still hesitate to don my wax-soled shoes. Suddenly, my old friend Jiezi returns from Jinling. Passing through Liangxi, he makes a brief stop, and sends a telegram inviting the renowned journalist Zhang Zhuping to come to Wuxi and travel together. The day Mr. Zhang arrived coincided with the Qingming Festival according to the old lunar calendar. After a long spell of rain, the weather suddenly cleared, and a gentle breeze blew. My spring travel plans, stirred by the arrival of a distinguished guest, were suddenly set in motion. Accompanying Zhang were his wife Yunqing, Miss Zhu Yidi, and Miss Zhang Huanfen, the principal of Rong's Girls' School, all of whom I had known for some time. We arranged a banquet at the Da Xin Restaurant to welcome them, and also invited Mr. and Mrs. Tang Moubo Yu Qingtang to accompany us, as the guests and the Tangs had the bonds of being from the same hometown and schoolmates. Meeting old friends, our enjoyment was doubled. I and Tiao Fu Mengdie arrived last, intending to be hasty hosts but instead becoming unexpected guests. We then arranged an evening banquet at Plum Garden. In the afternoon, we went to the garden to make all the preparations. Jiezi accompanied the guests to Huishan Park to sample tea and then climbed Xishan Longguang Pagoda to take in the sights of Huilu. Then they passed through Zhang Lane to visit Dongda Pond, and then to Huanfen's villa, returning to the garden when tired.

A Romantic Tale of Red Beans

— Jing Mengdie

Since Wang Mojie wrote about the red bean, it has been known as the seed of longing and has been woven into the works of countless poets and lyricists throughout the ages. However, this plant originates from Lingnan, and it is not easy for us to see it. Only the residence of Qian Muzhai of Yushan has a red bean tree, hence the name Red Bean Villa and the self-appellation Red Bean Elder. To this day, the tree still stands, surpassing any old family's tall trees. One evening after Qingming, my friend Xie Jiezi hosted guests in Wuxi at the Plum Garden. Among the guests was Mr. Yang, who took out a pair of red beans from his pocket, saying he had just bought them from Yushan. The pair of beans were brightly red and adorable, round and flat in shape, and as shiny as coral. The guests passed them around for viewing. Mr. Yang told me that each pod of this bean produces one seed, but occasionally there are two seeds. Their shapes also vary in size. Only those that are of the same size and come from the same pod are considered a pair of red beans, hence they are especially rare and precious. It is said among scholars that if a husband and wife each wear one of a pair of red beans, they will be husband and wife for generations to come, which is even better than the inlaid box in the Hall of Eternal Life. Is it the owner's story and promotion of the beans that make them rare, or is it the deep affection between the couple that makes them a symbol of unity, creating an indissoluble bond, or is it something inherent in the beans themselves? It is certainly better than wearing daylilies to wish for sons or Albizia flowers to dispel worries. This is the first time in my life that I have seen red beans, and Jiezi happened to ask for a poem about red beans. I wrote about red beans and then saw red beans. Such a wonderful coincidence, could it be a predestined connection? However, with princes and fragrant grasses, travelers at the ends of the earth, urgent urgings of spring, and a wild wind sweeping the scene, the peach blossoms have all fallen, the swallows have not returned, the red bean poem is complete, and my green shirt is wet with tears. I send it to Juan Gong for confirmation, fearing that the soul of the cuckoo will be emaciated and that my dream of butterflies will be confused, both sharing the same feeling of sadness for spring.

Slow Tune of Double Red Beans (Following Jiezi's rhyme, the original poem was previously published in this column) Deep spring in the south, news from the east wind is cut off. A tree full of longing. Remembering songs in the palace, lyrics spread in the boudoir. The joyous and sorrowful events, only the lover knows. It is hard to maintain the thread, a vain entanglement of a wisp of infatuation. Two branches sprout from the heart, like weeping pearls, congealing on the pillow. Seeing the mandarin ducks being driven away, the parrot is fed leftovers. The child only knows how to steal pleasures. More sorrow is planted in the womb, the more delicate, the more hesitant. The sweet dream returns, picking it up again, the gentle soul wants to fly. Comforting the estranged, adding to a small ailing life.

People Without Birthdays

— Ying Dai

▲ A Major Problem Amidst the Call for Calendar Reform

In Western countries, the calendar reform committee, seeking to unify the world's calendar, has recently created a new calendar with thirteen months in a year, each month with twenty-eight days. There is one extra day, which is a public holiday. It has now been decided to implement it from January 1933. However, once this calendar is implemented, people whose birthdays fall after the twenty-eighth, on the twenty-ninth, thirtieth, or thirty-first, will have no birthday to celebrate. And in the future, babies born on a public holiday will have no way to name their month and day.

February in the Gregorian calendar has twenty-eight days, with a leap year every four years, and twenty-nine days in a leap year. However, people born on February 29th only have a birthday once every four years, which Westerners consider unfortunate. With the new calendar, people born after the twenty-eighth will never have a birthday, which is surely a great misfortune. This is also a major problem amidst the call for calendar reform.

Chrysanthemum Cultivation Improvement Method

— Xiao Lei

Chrysanthemums of various colors will now be propagated by division and cuttings. As the saying goes, "Don't ask about the harvest, just ask about the cultivation." This applies to growing grains, and it also applies to growing ornamental flowers. In the past, gardeners often broke off the heads of chrysanthemum branches, about three feet long, some only four inches, and planted them in clusters in pots. After they sprouted roots, they would then divide them and plant one branch per pot. After planting, their vitality was often hampered for half a month, because the roots were separated from the soil during division and were injured. Last year, I heard that someone was good at growing chrysanthemums, making them large and flowery, so I visited him and asked him to teach me his good method. He said, "It's not difficult, just correct the gardener's mistakes. It's better to plant one branch per pot, without transplanting, to avoid repeated damage. Mix three parts chaff into the soil (the chaff from rice mills, usually used for feeding pigs). The pot should be larger so that the roots can stretch. Break off a chrysanthemum branch about four inches long and remove the top, about an inch or so, and then insert it into the pot. It will take root in half a month. Since the top was removed earlier, three branches will sprout. After the three branches have grown slightly, remove the tops of the three branches again, so that each branch will sprout three branches, for a total of nine branches. Each will have a terminal flower, so a total of nine flowers can bloom. The chaff mixed into the soil earlier is fertilizer. Later, fertilize it again, and the nine flowers will be large and different from ordinary ones. Now that the spring rain is like ointment, and the chrysanthemum buds are plump, the day for picking and inserting chrysanthemum heads is near. I am relaying what I heard from a chrysanthemum grower to those who are addicted to the eastern fence."

Bedbugs Kill People

— Wei

I have often talked about bedbugs. Although the insects are small, their harm is significant enough to kill. Someone named Qi, ten years ago when his master was still alive, was addicted to opium. Every night, he would not sleep until two or three o'clock, and he would order a maid to stay by his side to serve him. The maid, A Cui, was only twelve or thirteen years old, and she could not hold out in the middle of the night. She would often doze off in a rattan-bound armchair in front of the opium couch. This went on for more than two years. A Cui's face was bloodless, and she looked haggard. She thought it was caused by insomnia. At that time, the master treated his servants like animals and did not care. Later, she became more and more haggard and eventually died. The master, thinking of the chair in front of the couch as something A Cui had sat and slept on before her death, planned to move it elsewhere. This chair had not been moved for more than ten years. When the chair was moved and the cushion fell off, he saw a wriggling mass inside. Upon closer inspection, it was bedbugs. He did not know how many there were. He scooped them up and got about a liter's worth. He burned the chair along with them. Only then did he realize that A Cui's death was actually due to the bites of bedbugs. Her blood had been gradually sucked dry. He had often seen her twitching her body when she was dozing off. She was young and ignorant and did not try to catch them. She was overworked and had her blood sucked. After years of accumulation, how could she not die? How unjust!

Travel Notes from Southeast Asia (13)

— Ling Hua

▲ From Saigon to Singapore

On the morning of February 18th, at six o'clock, the ship left Saigon. Men and women on the shore were seeing us off. But since this is French territory, most of those boarding the ship are French, very few are British, and none are Chinese. This is strange. Besides me and Mr. Chen Kaiqing, there was only one female doctor, Kuang Cibei. Kuang's father is the director of the Dongshan Hospital in Guangzhou. Eleven members of her family are in the medical profession. Her sister is now in France. Although Kuang has already obtained a doctor's certificate in China, she still wants to study in Germany. She said that her sister has already rented a room for her in France, and the monthly rent is only about 30 Chinese silver dollars.

Life on a ship at sea is another kind of life. Mail ships are considered superior ships. The first and second class cabins are luxuriously decorated with fresh flowers. They are served by Western maids, like the use of maids in Japan. There are movie theaters, concerts, and dance halls. In the chairs, one can whistle to the sea and sky, or play various games on the deck. The square is boundless. The men and women are all sea immortals. The third class cabins also have electric fans, running water, and a large dining room. Ladies and gentlemen can read, write, and play the organ. The fourth class is also comparable to the cabins on the Yangtze River. As for the foreign workers and sailors, their lives and clothing are still crude, far from equal. The room servants are mostly Chinese on ships that travel through China and Southeast Asia and around the world. Unfortunately, they all speak Min and Cantonese, which are not easy to understand. But we cannot help but admire the creative power of the Min and Cantonese people in the world. Wherever there is sunlight, there are overseas Chinese, even in Australia. And most of the overseas Chinese are Min and Cantonese. Their employment as room servants allows them to travel the globe, implicitly occupying a major force in the world labor sector. Isn't that great?

On the 19th, the climate south of Saigon was completely summer. Saigon is already ten degrees north of the tropics. Traveling further south, the lined clothes could no longer be worn, and no one wore long clothes. On the ship, there were Indians who wore a long cloth skirt over their right shoulder, the color was light black, and their heads were wrapped in colored floral cloth. They sat in the scattered cabins, supported by cloth tents. Some could speak Chinese. Mr. Chen Kaiqing said that Indian businessmen are good at business. In Burma, there is a Chinese street, and the Indians face them in business, but the Chinese all fail. I asked, "Is it because the Indians are united in resisting the Chinese?" He said, "No, it's a natural failure." I asked, "Why?" He said, "They are very frugal in employing people, eating bread and drinking water, more diligent and thrifty than the Chinese. They also don't care much about appearances. They don't pay attention to the appearance of their houses and living quarters. Our Chinese are a little more wealthy, so we become lax and pay attention to appearances. We are also generous to our employees. As a result, the Chinese business fails, and the Indian business becomes rich." I said, "What will they do after they become rich?" He replied, "They also lack knowledge, and they only seek more wealth, and they are still stingy." I said, "This is what Westerners call a Jew. The Western meaning of a Jew is a money slave, referring to their lack of other thoughts. Looking at the efforts of Jews and Indians to get rich, and the lack of national and cultural movements, our nation must encourage itself. If the country and culture are not competitive, even if you are rich, you are still a slave, which is sad. I especially hope that the rich people of our country pay attention to this."

Warmth in the Heart (171)

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 10: The Scarlet Flames Leap to the Sky, the Courtesan Is a Filial Daughter; Red Carpet on the Ground, Meeting Celebrated Actors Instantly. At that time, many people also opened the water taps in the kitchen courtyards and filled buckets with water to pour on the fire. It was truly a drop in the bucket. Many neighbors also neglected the matter of putting out the fire. They only cared about moving their own boxes and belongings from their homes. The alleys were already crowded with many people, and adding to that were the objects being moved out by each family. Some were casually placed in the alleys. The objects being moved out were not complete items. Bedding and quilts were rolled together, and the items from the bed were scattered on the ground. Some also took down the curtains. For a time, the sounds of shouts big and small mixed together. Ruiyun's mother and aunt were anxious, constantly chanting "Amitabha, Amitabha," and complaining to A Jin, "Why are you still just watching? Why don't you help me pack the boxes?" A Jin said, "I'm so anxious that I don't know where to start. Which box should I pack?" At this time, Ruiyun returned, luckily having removed all her jewelry and hair ornaments and placed them in a small official box. This small official box was locked, and the key was always kept by the aunt. That had always been the case. A Jin said, "Then is your jewelry box packed?" The aunt said, "It's already packed." A Jin said, "That's good. Your property is all in this jewelry box anyway." The aunt said, "There are also clothes. Can't we just ignore them? Anan's clothes are not few either." A Jin said, "Where can we find time to pack those clothes now?" Zuo Shichen said, "Pack the important things. Let the unimportant things be. The Shanghai fire department is very fast. In a moment, the fire truck will arrive. This place is still separated by a small alley and two houses. I think it's all right." Just as he was speaking, they heard a series of ringing bells. Everyone said that the Municipal Council's fire truck had arrived. They saw many foreigners and Chinese in the fire department wearing golden copper helmets and fire-fighting uniforms, with leather boots that extended over their knees. They arrived in the alley and drove away the idle people who were watching the fire, clearing a path and dragging in a very thick leather hose. They attached it to the water tap. In a moment, they saw the leather hose, which was originally flat, gradually become full and fat, turning into a round bamboo tube. First, several firefighters placed ladders on the overhanging buildings, and one by one they went up, with axes and chisels attached to their waists. The windows were originally closed, but with one axe, they were split open. They inserted the leather hose. Other hoses also sucked up enough water and sprayed it towards the side where the fire was leaping out. In a moment, the fire's momentum weakened, and the fire's power subsided. Ruiyun and her group of little sisters were still children after all. They had never seen Shanghai fire fighting before. They stood on the veranda and found it amusing. They weren't anxious at all. As the saying goes, "It's fun to watch a fire burn, but it's hard on the people who are being affected."

Long-term Transaction Summary

The six pairs of long-term deposits and loans opened in September last year will generally expire this month. The details were once described in this newspaper, and most of the long-term settlements that expired on the 10th were also recorded in this newspaper. Today (the 15th), there is another large batch expiring. Furthermore, Ningbo banks have sent personnel to Shanghai to handle the handover and settlement issues. The following is a classified summary of the long-term news from various sources:

▲ Disposition of Expired Funds. Today is another major expiration date. For those that are due for settlement, the audited amount reaches 7 to 8 million. There are no fewer than 100 stores and small banks in Shanghai, each with hundreds of thousands or over a million. According to insiders yesterday, the internal silver root feels constricted due to this, stores with a lot of money are certainly not few but because of preventive plans also do not dare to open fully, and those short of silver are everywhere therefore it is necessary to recover this loan and put it back out, but long term of customer deposit still needs to choose the trustworthy one to pay so the old clients are recovered and released to new clients therefore handover in and out is more frequent this session, and transfers are actually limited, but the small banks, there is a lot of head lining, or there may be a slight overflow, which is also unknown.

▲ Gathering of Ningbo Banks. Most Ningbo banks have plenty of silver. It is heard that Ningbo banks want to continue to roll over as usual because Shanghai banks are unwilling to be responsible for lending due to the poor market so it is still questionable whether it will be recovered for now. It must wait until after the 25th before a decision can be made.

▲ The Out-of-Town Gangs Are Unable to Repay. The out-of-town gangs that are due to repay long-term loans are unable to do so as scheduled due to poor business and the market being affected by foreign exchange and various other factors, causing a large amount of receivables that have not yet circulated. As a result, they cannot repay the bank loans as scheduled. Bond Prices Mostly Up, Few Down

Yesterday, spot transactions amounted to 30,000 yuan, including 10,000 yuan of demobilization bonds and 8,000 yuan of customs duties bonds, with other transactions only reaching several thousand yuan. The futures market saw sluggish trading, with approximately 1.8 million in customs duties bonds, about 1 million in demobilization bonds, nearly 800,000 in rehabilitation bonds, 60,000 yuan in series 6, 560,000 yuan in reorganization series 6, over 300,000 yuan in series 25, and around 100,000 yuan each in 7-year, 96, and disarmament bonds. Only 15,000 yuan of financial bonds were traded this month. Prices for 7-year, 96, and series 25 bonds were particularly stable, fluctuating only by 1-2 jiao throughout the day, with minimal changes compared to the previous week. Other bonds, driven by active buying, generally trended upward, resulting in gains of around 0.5 yuan. Reorganization series 6 saw the most significant fluctuations, with the May futures rising by 1.1 yuan, and the April futures and spot prices also rising by 0.7-0.8 yuan, showing stronger momentum compared to other bonds.

Yarn & Cotton: Political Instability the Only Obstacle to Yarn Sales

The yarn market is weak and trending downward, mainly due to political tensions and sluggish current sales, leading to softening sentiment. Even if prices rise, they lack sustained momentum. However, actual manufacturers remain firm and unwilling to relax their stance, while major sellers also hold out, leading to fierce competition between bulls and bears. Some retail shorts have been adding to their positions in recent months, so the outlook for this month remains highly uncertain.

▲Near-Term Yarn Prices Drop by One or Two Taels. In the morning session, prices for July remained tight, with few sellers. Around 2-3 PM, news of poor yarn sales emerged, with Grade 3 flat and a lack of buyers, leading to a loosening of the market. Prices for various months fell by 2, 3, 5, and 6 qian. The afternoon saw a further weakening of the market and increased selling pressure. Prices for the current month fell by one or two taels, and prices for later months fell by 1, 4, and 5 qian. Trading volume was not strong. Total daily transactions were 13,455 bales. The closing prices are recorded below:

Variety　Closing Price　Change　Inventory　Closing Price　Change　Inventory

April　151.0　Down 1.2　38,350　July　152.1　Down 9　24,050

May　151.7　Down 1.3　40,650　August　152.57　　19,100

June　152.0　　8　31,300　September　153.25　　6,350

▲Current Yarn Outlets Flat. Total daily purchases by various groups were 880 bales. Purchases by fellow traders were 250 bales. Among the customer groups, Sichuan saw the strongest volume, with 425 bales. In addition, Guangdong purchased 305 bales, the interior 70 bales, Shantou 35 bales, and other miscellaneous groups 55 bales. Market sentiment was flat.

Cotton Market Sees Sharp Decline

The cotton market has softened, with a significant downward trend. This is mainly due to the cooling of the overseas cotton market, sluggish sales of current cotton in the market, and weak factory demand, leading to slightly fatigued sentiment. Profiteers are liquidating their positions, causing the market to loosen.

▲Futures Cotton Drops by Three Qian. The morning session saw the Hankou futures market open with a subdued mood due to the flatness of the overseas cotton market and a lack of buying interest. As liquidations increased, prices for various months fell sharply by 2.5 to 3.5 qian. In the afternoon, profiteers covered their short positions, leading to a slight recovery. As a result, prices for various months changed by 5 fen to 1 qian. Total daily transactions were 36,900 dan. The closing prices are recorded below:

Grains: Rainy Weather Causes Sluggish Rice Market

▲Zhabei Yesterday, the arrival of goods from various sources remained quiet, and river inventories remained undiminished. The North Japonica market was increasingly sluggish, with weak top-grade transactions. Medium-grade rice showed slight movement, and prices recovered slightly. There were signs of stabilization at noon. Both arrivals and sales of thin Indica rice were sluggish, and high-grade rice also shifted downstream, with few customers for medium and lower grades. River shipments of sheep Indica rice were particularly scarce, and sales were normal, but the overall market was stable. Sales of Duzi rice at customer ports were still acceptable, but inventories were dwindling, and prices remained unchanged. Sales of common inferior rice were slow and stagnant, and the situation was extremely dull with no change. Overall, rice trading was weak throughout the day, and prices trended flat.

▲South Shanghai River shipments remained scarce, and sales were selectively made to rural villages. After consecutive declines in recent days, sales of Suzhou and Tongxiang Japonica rice showed slight movement, and high prices seemed stable. Lower-grade rice continued to decline. Arrivals and inventories of Changzhou and Wuxi high-grade Japonica rice were low, and merchants were taking a wait-and-see approach due to high prices. The market trend continued to be sluggish, and the price level remained unchanged. Customer groups showed some interest in Southern thin Indica and early Indica rice, but they were very picky, and market prices were only slightly lower in wholesale. Sales of sheep Duzi rice were flat. Recently, most shops selling imported rice have adequately stocked their inventories, and prices are stable. Sales of white rice were unsatisfactory, but distilleries slightly increased purchases of top-grade inferior rice, although market prices remained average.

Futures Low-Grade Rice Continues to Rise

Yesterday's imported rice market continued to show a favorable trend with customer groups paying close attention. However, spot rice transactions were limited due to incoming shipments, and prices only rose by a few cents. 2,000 bags of Saigon No. 2 were offered at 14.91 yuan, 2,000 bags of low-grade rice were offered at 14.68 yuan, 2,000 bags of Min Dang rice were offered at 14.78 yuan, and 600 bags of brown rice were offered at 14.29 yuan. Saigon No. 1 had high inventories and slow sales, with 1,000 bags offered at 15.45 yuan, and medium and lower grades were discounted.

Imported rice futures markets were bullish, and sellers were reluctant to offer much. Domestic appetite was strong, and returning shipments became increasingly firm. Low-grade rice continued to rise, with prices of two to eight cents per bag, with only 1,500 tons offered.

Rainy Weather Boosts Flour Market

Yesterday morning's flour market saw April and May prices open lower due to reports of low overseas wheat prices (0.5-0.7 yuan), causing temporary weakness in sentiment. However, new crop prices for later months were not affected by the reports of low overseas wheat prices, maintaining their high interest. Due to the heavy rain the previous night and the clear weather yesterday, sentiment both inside and outside the market was greatly stimulated, and buying interest was strong. Many were concerned that abundant harvests would not materialize, and the current weather conditions confirmed their fears. The buying interest increased further in the afternoon, and trading was particularly active. Some Suzhou and most Jiangsu groups were covering their short positions, causing market prices to rise. The market shift due to weather conditions is a common occurrence, but this year's sentiment is even more intense. Near-term contracts remain stable due to unchanged actual sales. As a result, the current month is up 0.025 yuan compared to the previous day, May is up 0.01 yuan, June and July are up 0.0175 yuan, and August and September are expected to rise by 0.02 yuan.

Distant New Wheat Surges 0.08 Yuan

Yesterday, futures wheat and flour sales were poor, and current inventories were high, with little enthusiasm. Distant new wheat, however, saw unusual excitement due to continuous spring rain and cold weather, especially for June contracts. Due to excessive spring rain, the abundance of the harvest cannot be predicted, but delays are expected, leading to increased market focus. Nanjing and Jiangsu groups were selling heavily, leading to heavy short covering and rising market prices. As a result, the current month closed 0.01 yuan lower than the previous week, June rose a massive 0.08 yuan, July rose 0.03 yuan, August rose 0.04 yuan, and September rose 0.03 yuan. Current wheat transactions were weak, and prices were stable. High-quality goods seemed slightly lower than the previous week due to the firm stance of factories. Five taels and 0.16 yuan was offered for Southern Suzhou wheat, 5.16 yuan for Qingjiangpu wheat, 5.16 yuan for Bengbu and Xuzhou wheat, and 5.01 to 5.03 yuan for Mingguang wheat. A total of 14,000 bags were handled by Fuxin.

Piece Goods: Spring Rain Causes Quiet Piece Goods Sales

▲Local Cotton Cloth: Rainy weather means no customers. Wholesale is slow. Coarse cloth remains unchanged. Over a hundred pieces of 11-pound cloth were traded in Ningbo, Hangzhou and other ports, with Three Rabbits being the strongest, opening at 4.65 taels. Three Cats and Three Deer at 4.6 taels have already been sold. Heavy cloth is slightly softer due to lack of movement in the northern market. However, 17-pound Five Bats is particularly strong due to low inventory. Coarse twill is increasingly dull. Medium blue fine twill double fish at 0.025, opening at 6.5 taels, Yang Crane spot goods are still short. The rising trend of fine cloth is not yet over. Over 150 pieces were purchased by Wenzhou, Taizhou and other groups yesterday.

▲Eastern and Western Piece Goods: Continuous spring rain has led to a weakening market. Sluggish actual sales are rare in recent years. Customer groups show no interest in replenishment, and replenishment in the local market is limited. Eastern goods have already begun to decline. Raw Western Yarn has fallen by 0.025 yuan. Dian Qiuxiang opened at 8.425 taels, Tang Taizong at 8.25 taels, Zijinshan at 8 taels. It is observed that an increasing number of 84 cloth is being redyed, making it difficult to maintain stability. Medium Mokanshan, Hunter Goose Muqiu of upright tribute Nima has returned to 0.2625 yuan. However, Double Child Deer is at 0.235 yuan because of its low stock. Recently, white straight-stripe hemp yarn and blue straight-stripe hemp yarn of Western goods have fallen consistently. However, fifty pieces of bleached cloth have been purchased by northern groups. Gongping chased Qiuxiang to 8.85 taels, and Flying Kite to 8.4 taels.

Silk & Tea: Chinese Silk Shipments to the US Surge

▲Over 80,000 Bales Shipped Since Last Summer, Up Over 30,000 Bales. Our country's silk has always been a major export commodity. Each year, 80,000-90,000 bales are shipped from Shanghai, mostly to the Americas. In recent years, the sales of silk fabrics in the United States have been increasing daily, and the consumption of raw silk has been growing. Last autumn, due to the lifting of the gold embargo in Japan, the gold market soared and silver prices were extremely low. American silk merchants abandoned Japanese silk for Chinese silk (silk trade with Japan uses gold, while with China uses silver, making Chinese silk cheaper). Chinese silk exports to the US surged. Since the new silk market opened last summer, shipments of Chinese silk from the Shanghai Customs to the United States have totaled 89,765 bales, a massive increase of 34,688 bales compared to the same period last year.

British and French Follow Suit to Purchase Futures Silk

Yesterday's foreign silk market in Shanghai continued to show prosperity. Since the US firms heavily replenished their stock last week due to shortages, silk inventories in the market are even lower. British and French firms followed suit to purchase, and Indian firms also traded yellow and white coarse silk. Market sentiment was firm and prosperous. Yesterday, Xinfu and others imported 50 bales of Shanghai White Factory silk, Zhonghe and others imported 20 bales of White Qian silk, and Kechang and others imported 19 bales of yellow coarse silk. Prices are increasingly firm.

Group News

▲The Yiqun Small Football Team announced that their team invited the Wuchang team for a friendly match at 9 AM yesterday (the 13th) at the YMCA field. Referee Xu Shichang blew the whistle, and the players from both sides vigorously started the game. The Yiqun team was calm and effective in both offense and defense. Huang Guixuan scored the first goal, and Yiqun led 2-1 in the first half. After the break, they changed sides to play. The Wuchang team was not weak, and tried to counterattack, but failed to cooperate and missed several opportunities. As a result, Yiqun won 8-3. Also, at 10:30 AM on the same day, they accepted the invitation of the Puxing team. Yiqun led 2-1 in the first half. In the second half, the weather turned bad, with light rain falling and the field becoming wet. The referee blew the whistle to stop the game and announced a postponement, which both sides agreed to. The game will be played next week.

Commercial News

▲The Huilo Company on Nanjing Road and Sichuan Road announced that their piece goods department recently received a large number of fabrics for women's clothing for the spring and summer seasons, such as Moonlight brand linen with dozens of colors, with a width of 2.7 chi, and selling for only 1.5 yuan per yard. This yarn will not change color even after being steamed and boiled in boiling water for ten hours. The female staff of the department are all wearing this material to prove it. Also, silk-like iron blood silk is solid, durable and washable, and has no crease problems. The designs are new and very pleasing to the eye, with over 50 types, and the price is between 2.95 yuan and 4.5 yuan per yard. There are also new styles of wool yarn for summer, which are light, soft, fine and clean, with many colors. Over 200 styles have been recently shipped, and the price is between 2.25 yuan and 2.75 yuan per yard. Women have been coming in crowds to purchase them in recent days.

▲The Hongzhang Silk Satin Shop in Xiaodongmen announced that since adding the foreign goods department, customers have found it convenient. The shop held an official grand opening sale last month, and despite the continuous rain, customers still came in droves, and the scene was as lively as ever. The new spring fabrics for women's clothing have the most unique designs among the shops in the area. Ms. Jiang Wanzhen, a famous lady from Suzhou, also visited the shop with her mother yesterday and purchased a large number of various new fabrics. She particularly praised the Hongzhang silk and Fanhua satin invented by the shop.

▲Guangshengxiang announced that since relocating from Zhejiang Road to No. 5 Mashan Street and Zhongshan Street, the shop has been open since the 10th of this month. Although there was heavy rain that day, it was still very crowded. Hundreds of pieces of 13-chi Guangdong woolen fabric at 1.6 yuan per piece were sold. A lot of silk wool crepe at 0.48 yuan per chi and adding two extra feet were also sold. Buyers were all satisfied.

Theater News

▲ Star Film Company announced that it has been exclusively commissioned by the Hangzhou National Games to produce the event's sports film. The company dispatched several photographers with multiple new-style cameras to capture footage, from the opening to the closing ceremonies. The resulting film is over 12,000 feet long, encompassing various men's and women's sports performances in detail. The Games also entrusted the company with exclusive distribution rights for the film. The company has already agreed with the Central Grand Theater to premiere the film in Shanghai as soon as possible, and the exact screening dates will be announced shortly.

▲ Golden Grand Theater announced that the film "Angel," starring Charles Farrell and Janet Gaynor, vividly and profoundly depicts the relationship between life and love. Its poignant beauty makes it an unprecedented masterpiece in the film industry. The Golden has been showing this film for several consecutive days, and ticket sales have not decreased due to the rain. The film will only be shown for today and tomorrow, and the day after tomorrow, it will be replaced by "Storm in the Forbidden City."

▲ Paris Grand Theater announced that from today, it will be showing "The Phantom of the Pleasure Garden," a masterpiece by the renowned makeup artist, Lon Chaney. The film portrays the dark side of society and the bitterness of the underworld, filled with ingenious amusement. Chaney's performance in the film surpasses his role in "The Hunchback of Notre Dame." As the theater has many blockbuster films lined up, "The Phantom of the Pleasure Garden" will only be shown for three days. Those who love watching excellent films should not miss this opportunity.

▲ Nangong Drama Society announced that all of its facilities and arrangements have been completed. The entire society decided in a general meeting yesterday to hold its first public performance on May 17th at the Shanghai Grand Theater. The program will include Mr. Zheng Baiqi's "Crisis," Shaw's "Man and Superman" for European drama, and Mr. Guo Moruo's "Zhuo Wenjun" for classical drama. The rehearsals have been directed by the head of drama affairs, Mao Bixin, with Mai Mengxia and Zhuo Huilun in charge of different roles.

▲ Fox Star Film Company announced that the film "Pirate's Blood," directed by Lu Fuyue, has been praised by all who have seen it. The long-awaited martial arts and special effects blockbuster "Cavalry Knight" was fully completed last month. The entire plot focuses on martial arts and love. Director Lu Fuyue used [blank space] techniques to direct this masterpiece. The female lead, Qian Siying (as Huijuan), and the male lead, Huang Qigu Song, both delivered perfect performances. The film will be released in major theaters in Shanghai soon.
